	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">South America</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Southern America" redirects here. For the region of the United States of America, see <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">Southern United States</a>. For the botanical continent defined in the World Geographical Scheme for Recording Plant Distributions, see <a href="/wiki/Southern_America_(WGSRPD)" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern America (WGSRPD)">Southern America (WGSRPD)</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">A continent in the Western Hemisphere, and mostly in the Southern Hemisphere</div>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. <p><b>South America</b>  is a <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">continent</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>, mostly in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>, with a relatively small portion in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern Hemisphere</a>. It may also be considered a <a href="/wiki/Subcontinent" class="mw-redirect" title="Subcontinent">subcontinent</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-britannica-southamerica_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-southamerica-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> which is how it is viewed in the Spanish and Portuguese-speaking regions of the Americas. The reference to South America instead of other regions (like <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cone" title="Southern Cone">Southern Cone</a>) has increased in the last decades due to changing geopolitical dynamics (in particular, the rise of Brazil).<sup id="cite_ref-academia.edu_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-academia.edu-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs additional references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">additional citation(s) needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>It is bordered on the west by the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> and on the north and east by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>; <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> lie to the northwest. It includes twelve sovereign states (<a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>), a <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_France" title="Regions of France">part</a> of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (<a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>), and a non-sovereign area (the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a>, a <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territory" class="mw-redirect" title="British Overseas Territory">British Overseas Territory</a> though this is <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands_sovereignty_dispute" title="Falkland Islands sovereignty dispute">disputed</a> by Argentina). In addition to this, the <a href="/wiki/ABC_islands_(Lesser_Antilles)" title="ABC islands (Lesser Antilles)">ABC islands</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a> may also be considered part of South America.
</p><p>South America has an <a href="/wiki/Area" title="Area">area</a> of 17,840,000 square kilometers (6,890,000 sq mi). Its <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">population</a> as of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> has been estimated at more than 420 million.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> South America <a href="/wiki/List_of_continents_by_population" title="List of continents by population">ranks fourth</a> in area (after <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, and North America) and fifth in population (after Asia, Africa, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, and North America). Brazil is by far the most populous South American country, with more than half of the continent's population, followed by Colombia, Argentina, Venezuela and Peru. In recent decades Brazil has also concentrated half of the region's GDP and has become a first regional power.<sup id="cite_ref-academia.edu_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-academia.edu-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Most of the population lives near the continent's western or eastern coasts while the interior and the <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">far south</a> are sparsely populated. The geography of western South America is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> mountains; in contrast, the eastern part contains both highland regions and vast lowlands where rivers such as the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orinoco" title="Orinoco">Orinoco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_River" title="Paraná River">Paraná</a> flow. Most of the continent lies in the <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">tropics</a>.
</p><p>The continent's cultural and ethnic outlook has its origin with the interaction of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous peoples</a> with European conquerors and immigrants and, more locally, with African slaves. Given a long <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">history of colonialism</a>, the overwhelming majority of South Americans speak <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> or <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, and societies and states reflect <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western traditions</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_South_America" title="Geography of South America">Geography of South America</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Environment_of_South_America" title="Category:Environment of South America">Category:Environment of South America</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:South_America_-_Blue_Marble_orthographic.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/South_America_-_Blue_Marble_orthographic.jpg/180px-South_America_-_Blue_Marble_orthographic.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/South_America_-_Blue_Marble_orthographic.jpg/270px-South_America_-_Blue_Marble_orthographic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/South_America_-_Blue_Marble_orthographic.jpg/360px-South_America_-_Blue_Marble_orthographic.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7200" data-file-height="10000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:South_America_-_Blue_Marble_orthographic.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A composite relief image of South America</div></div></div>
<p>South America occupies the southern portion of the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>. The continent is generally delimited on the northwest by the <a href="/wiki/Dari%C3%A9n_Gap" title="Darién Gap">Darién watershed</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Colombia%E2%80%93Panama_border" title="Colombia–Panama border">Colombia–Panama border</a>, although some may consider the border instead to be the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">Panama Canal</a>. <a href="/wiki/Geopolitics" title="Geopolitics">Geopolitically</a> and geographically<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> all of <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>&#160;– including the segment east of the Panama Canal in the isthmus&#160;– is typically included in North America alone<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-North_America_Atlas_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-North_America_Atlas-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and among the <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Central_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Demographics of Central America">countries of Central America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Almost all of mainland South America sits on the <a href="/wiki/South_American_Plate" title="South American Plate">South American Plate</a>.
</p><p>South America is home to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_waterfalls_by_height" title="List of waterfalls by height">world's highest uninterrupted waterfall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angel_Falls" title="Angel Falls">Angel Falls</a> in Venezuela; the highest single drop waterfall <a href="/wiki/Kaieteur_Falls" title="Kaieteur Falls">Kaieteur Falls</a> in Guyana; the largest river by volume, the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon River</a>; the longest mountain range, the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> (whose highest mountain is <a href="/wiki/Aconcagua" title="Aconcagua">Aconcagua</a> at 6,962&#160;m or 22,841&#160;ft); the driest non-polar place on earth, the <a href="/wiki/Atacama_Desert" title="Atacama Desert">Atacama Desert</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> the largest rainforest, the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Rainforest" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Rainforest">Amazon Rainforest</a>; the highest capital city, <a href="/wiki/La_Paz,_Bolivia" class="mw-redirect" title="La Paz, Bolivia">La Paz, Bolivia</a>; the highest commercially navigable lake in the world, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Titicaca" title="Lake Titicaca">Lake Titicaca</a>; and, excluding research stations in <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a>, the world's southernmost permanently inhabited community, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Toro,_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Toro, Chile">Puerto Toro, Chile</a>.
</p><p>South America's major mineral resources are <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silver" title="Silver">silver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iron_ore" title="Iron ore">iron ore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a>. These resources found in South America have brought high income to its countries especially in times of war or of rapid economic growth by industrialized countries elsewhere. However, the concentration in producing one major export <a href="/wiki/Commodity" title="Commodity">commodity</a> often has hindered the development of diversified economies. The fluctuation in the price of commodities in the international markets has led historically to major highs and lows in the economies of South American states, often causing extreme political instability. This is leading to efforts to diversify production to drive away from staying as economies dedicated to one major export.
</p><p>South America is one of the most biodiverse continents on earth. South America is home to many interesting and unique species of animals including the <a href="/wiki/Llama" title="Llama">llama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anaconda" title="Anaconda">anaconda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piranha" title="Piranha">piranha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaguar" title="Jaguar">jaguar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicu%C3%B1a" title="Vicuña">vicuña</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tapir" title="Tapir">tapir</a>. The Amazon rainforests possess high <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>, containing a major proportion of the Earth's <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a>.
</p><p>Brazil is the largest country in South America, encompassing around half of the continent's land area and population. The remaining countries and territories are divided among three regions: The <a href="/wiki/Andean_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Andean States">Andean States</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Guianas" title="The Guianas">the Guianas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cone" title="Southern Cone">Southern Cone</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Outlying_islands">Outlying islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Outlying islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Traditionally, South America also includes some of the nearby islands. <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">Curaçao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_dependencies_of_Venezuela" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal dependencies of Venezuela">federal dependencies of Venezuela</a> sit on the northerly South American <a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">continental shelf</a> and are often considered part of the continent. Geo-politically, the island states and overseas territories of the Caribbean are generally grouped as a part or subregion of North America, since they are more distant on the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">Caribbean Plate</a>, even though <a href="/wiki/San_Andr%C3%A9s_(island)" title="San Andrés (island)">San Andres</a> and <a href="/wiki/Providencia_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Providencia Island">Providencia</a> are politically part of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aves_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Aves Island">Aves Island</a> is controlled by <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-North_America_Atlas_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-North_America_Atlas-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other islands that are included with South America are the <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">Galápagos Islands</a> that belong to <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a> and <a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">Easter Island</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a> but belonging to <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>), <a href="/wiki/Robinson_Crusoe_Island" title="Robinson Crusoe Island">Robinson Crusoe Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chilo%C3%A9_Archipelago" title="Chiloé Archipelago">Chiloé</a> (both Chilean) and <a href="/wiki/Tierra_del_Fuego" title="Tierra del Fuego">Tierra del Fuego</a> (split in between Chile and <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>). In the Atlantic, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> owns <a href="/wiki/Fernando_de_Noronha" title="Fernando de Noronha">Fernando de Noronha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trindade_and_Martim_Vaz" class="mw-redirect" title="Trindade and Martim Vaz">Trindade and Martim Vaz</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter_and_Saint_Paul_Archipelago" title="Saint Peter and Saint Paul Archipelago">Saint Peter and Saint Paul Archipelago</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> are governed by the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, whose sovereignty over the islands is <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands_sovereignty_dispute" title="Falkland Islands sovereignty dispute">disputed by Argentina</a>. <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands</a> may be associated with either South America or <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_South_America_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Koppen-Geiger_Map_South_America_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_South_America_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Koppen-Geiger_Map_South_America_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_South_America_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Koppen-Geiger_Map_South_America_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_South_America_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1294" data-file-height="850" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_South_America_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen-Geiger climate classification</a> map for South America.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tropical_cyclones_1945_2006_wikicolor.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Tropical_cyclones_1945_2006_wikicolor.png/220px-Tropical_cyclones_1945_2006_wikicolor.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Tropical_cyclones_1945_2006_wikicolor.png/330px-Tropical_cyclones_1945_2006_wikicolor.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Tropical_cyclones_1945_2006_wikicolor.png/440px-Tropical_cyclones_1945_2006_wikicolor.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1358" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tropical_cyclones_1945_2006_wikicolor.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of all tropical cyclone tracks from 1945 to 2006.</div></div></div>
<p>The distribution of the average temperatures in the region presents a constant regularity from the <a href="/wiki/30th_parallel_south" title="30th parallel south">30° of latitude south</a>, when the isotherms tend, more and more, to be confused with the degrees of latitude.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In temperate latitudes, <a href="/wiki/Winter" title="Winter">winters</a> are milder and <a href="/wiki/Summer" title="Summer">summers</a> warmer than in North America. Because its most extensive part of the continent is in the equatorial zone, the region has more areas of equatorial plains than any other region.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The average annual temperatures in the Amazon basin oscillate around 27&#160;°C (81&#160;°F), with low thermal amplitudes and high <a href="/wiki/Rainfall" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainfall">rainfall</a> indices. Between the <a href="/wiki/Maracaibo_Lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Maracaibo Lake">Maracaibo Lake</a> and the mouth of the Orinoco, predominates an <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Equatorial climate">equatorial climate</a> of the type Congolese, that also includes parts of the Brazilian territory.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The east-central Brazilian plateau has a humid and warm tropical climate. The northern and eastern parts of the Argentine pampas have a <a href="/wiki/Subtropics" title="Subtropics">humid subtropical climate</a> with dry winters and humid summers of the Chinese type, while the western and eastern ranges have a subtropical climate of the dinaric type. At the highest points of the Andean region, climates are colder than the ones occurring at the highest point of the Norwegian fjords. In the Andean plateaus, the warm climate prevails, although it is tempered by the altitude, while in the coastal strip, there is an equatorial climate of the Guinean type. From this point until the north of the Chilean coast appear, successively, <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean oceanic climate</a>, temperate of the Breton type and, already in <a href="/wiki/Tierra_del_Fuego" title="Tierra del Fuego">Tierra del Fuego</a>, cold climate of the Siberian type.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The distribution of rainfall is related to the regime of winds and air masses. In most of the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical region">tropical region</a> east of the Andes, winds blowing from the northeast, east and southeast carry moisture from the Atlantic, causing abundant rainfall. However, due to a consistently strong <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> and a weak <a href="/wiki/Intertropical_Convergence_Zone" title="Intertropical Convergence Zone">Intertropical Convergence Zone</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_tropical_cyclone" title="South Atlantic tropical cyclone">South Atlantic tropical cyclones</a> are rare.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Los_Llanos_(South_America)" title="Los Llanos (South America)">Orinoco Llanos</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/The_Guianas" title="The Guianas">Guianas plateau</a>, the precipitation levels go from moderate to high. The Pacific coast of Colombia and northern Ecuador are rainy regions, with <a href="/wiki/Choc%C3%B3" class="mw-redirect" title="Chocó">Chocó</a> in Colombia being the most rainy place in the world along with the northern slopes of Indian Himalayas.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The Atacama Desert, along this stretch of coast, is one of the driest regions in the world. The central and southern parts of Chile are subject to <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclones</a>, and most of the Argentine <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">Patagonia</a> is <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Pampas" title="Pampas">pampas</a> of Argentina, Uruguay and South of Brazil the rainfall is moderate, with rains well distributed during the year. The moderately dry conditions of the Chaco oppose the intense rainfall of the eastern region of Paraguay. In the <a href="/wiki/Semiarid" class="mw-redirect" title="Semiarid">semiarid</a> coast of the Brazilian Northeast the rains are linked to a monsoon regime.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Important factors in the determination of climates are sea currents, such as the current Humboldt and <a href="/wiki/Falklands" class="mw-redirect" title="Falklands">Falklands</a>. The equatorial current of the South Atlantic strikes the coast of the Northeast and there is divided into two others: the current of Brazil and a coastal current that flows to the northwest towards the <a href="/wiki/Antilles" title="Antilles">Antilles</a>, where there it moves towards northeast course thus forming the most Important and famous ocean current in the world, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_21-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Know.net_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Know.net-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_America" title="History of South America">History of South America</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_America#Pre-Columbian_era" title="History of South America">History of South America §&#160;Pre-Columbian era</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SantaCruz-CuevaManos-P2210651b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/SantaCruz-CuevaManos-P2210651b.jpg/220px-SantaCruz-CuevaManos-P2210651b.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/SantaCruz-CuevaManos-P2210651b.jpg/330px-SantaCruz-CuevaManos-P2210651b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/SantaCruz-CuevaManos-P2210651b.jpg/440px-SantaCruz-CuevaManos-P2210651b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SantaCruz-CuevaManos-P2210651b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The prehistoric <a href="/wiki/Cueva_de_las_Manos" title="Cueva de las Manos">Cueva de las Manos</a>, or "Cave of the Hands", in Argentina</div></div></div>
<p>South America is believed to have been joined with Africa from the late <a href="/wiki/Paleozoic_Era" class="mw-redirect" title="Paleozoic Era">Paleozoic Era</a> to the early <a href="/wiki/Mesozoic_Era" class="mw-redirect" title="Mesozoic Era">Mesozoic Era</a>, until the <a href="/wiki/Supercontinent" title="Supercontinent">supercontinent</a> <a href="/wiki/Pangaea" title="Pangaea">Pangaea</a> began to rift and break apart about 225 million years ago. Therefore, South America and Africa share similar fossils and rock layers.
</p><p>South America is thought to have been first inhabited by humans when people were crossing the <a href="/wiki/Beringia" title="Beringia">Bering Land Bridge</a> (now the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">Bering Strait</a>) at least 15,000 years ago from the territory that is present-day Russia. They migrated south through North America, and eventually reached South America through the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">Isthmus of Panama</a>.
</p><p>The first evidence for the existence of the human race in South America dates back to about 9000 BC, when <a href="/wiki/Squash_(plant)" class="mw-redirect" title="Squash (plant)">squashes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chili_pepper" title="Chili pepper">chili peppers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bean" title="Bean">beans</a> began to be cultivated for food in the highlands of the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Basin">Amazon Basin</a>. Pottery evidence further suggests that <a href="/wiki/Manioc" class="mw-redirect" title="Manioc">manioc</a>, which remains a <a href="/wiki/Staple_food" title="Staple food">staple food</a> today, was being cultivated as early as 2000 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-OBrienP-Oxford_Atlas_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OBrienP-Oxford_Atlas-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By 2000 BC, many <a href="/wiki/Agrarian_society" title="Agrarian society">agrarian</a> communities had been settled throughout the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> and the surrounding regions. Fishing became a widespread practice along the coast, helping establish fish as a primary source of food. Irrigation systems were also developed at this time, which aided in the rise of an <a href="/wiki/Agrarian_society" title="Agrarian society">agrarian society</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-OBrienP-Oxford_Atlas_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OBrienP-Oxford_Atlas-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>South American cultures began domesticating <a href="/wiki/Llama" title="Llama">llamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicu%C3%B1a" title="Vicuña">vicuñas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guanaco" title="Guanaco">guanacos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alpaca" title="Alpaca">alpacas</a> in the highlands of the Andes circa 3500 BC. Besides their use as sources of meat and wool, these animals were used for transportation of goods.<sup id="cite_ref-OBrienP-Oxford_Atlas_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OBrienP-Oxford_Atlas-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian_civilizations">Pre-Columbian civilizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Pre-Columbian civilizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era#South_America" title="Pre-Columbian era">Pre-Columbian era §&#160;South America</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Machu_Picchu,_Per%C3%BA,_2015-07-30,_DD_39.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_39.JPG/220px-Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_39.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_39.JPG/330px-Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_39.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_39.JPG/440px-Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_39.JPG 2x" data-file-width="6399" data-file-height="5496" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Machu_Picchu,_Per%C3%BA,_2015-07-30,_DD_39.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Inca estate of <a href="/wiki/Machu_Picchu" title="Machu Picchu">Machu Picchu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> is one of the <a href="/wiki/New_Seven_Wonders_of_the_World#Winners" class="mw-redirect" title="New Seven Wonders of the World">New Seven Wonders of the World</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The rise of plant growing and the subsequent appearance of permanent human settlements allowed for the multiple and overlapping beginnings of civilizations in South America.
</p><p>One of the earliest known South American civilizations was at <a href="/wiki/Norte_Chico_civilization" title="Norte Chico civilization">Norte Chico</a>, on the central <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peruvian</a> coast. Though a pre-ceramic culture, the monumental architecture of Norte Chico is contemporaneous with the pyramids of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Ancient Egypt</a>. Norte Chico governing class established a trade network and developed agriculture then followed by <a href="/wiki/Chavin_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Chavin culture">Chavín</a> by 900 BC, according to some estimates and archaeological finds. Artifacts were found at a site called <a href="/wiki/Chav%C3%ADn_de_Huantar" title="Chavín de Huantar">Chavín de Huantar</a> in modern Peru at an elevation of 3,177 meters (10,423&#160;ft). Chavín civilization spanned 900 BC to 300 BC.
</p><p>In the central coast of Peru, around the beginning of the 1st millennium AD, <a href="/wiki/Moche_(culture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Moche (culture)">Moche</a> (100 BC&#160;– 700 AD, at the northern coast of Peru), <a href="/wiki/Paracas_culture" title="Paracas culture">Paracas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nazca_culture" title="Nazca culture">Nazca</a> (400 BC&#160;– 800 AD, Peru) cultures flourished with centralized states with permanent militia improving agriculture through <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigation</a> and new styles of ceramic art. At the <a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">Altiplano</a>, Tiahuanaco or <a href="/wiki/Tiwanaku" title="Tiwanaku">Tiwanaku</a> (100 BC&#160;– 1200 AD, Bolivia) managed a large commercial network based on religion.
</p><p>Around the 7th century, both Tiahuanaco and Wari or <a href="/wiki/Wari_culture" title="Wari culture">Huari</a> Empire (600–1200, Central and northern Peru) expanded its influence to all the Andean region, imposing the Huari urbanism and Tiahuanaco religious iconography.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Muisca_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Muisca people">Muisca</a> were the main indigenous civilization in what is now Colombia. They established the <a href="/wiki/Muisca_Confederation" title="Muisca Confederation">Muisca Confederation</a> of many clans, or <i><a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">cacicazgos</a></i>, that had a free trade network among themselves. They were goldsmiths and farmers.
</p><p>Other important Pre-Columbian cultures include: the <a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1ari" title="Cañari">Cañaris</a> (in south central Ecuador), <a href="/wiki/Chim%C3%BA_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Chimú Empire">Chimú Empire</a> (1300–1470, Peruvian northern coast), <a href="/wiki/Chachapoyas_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Chachapoyas culture">Chachapoyas</a>, and the Aymaran kingdoms (1000–1450, Western Bolivia and southern Peru).
Holding their capital at the great city of <a href="/wiki/Cusco" title="Cusco">Cusco</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Inca_civilization" class="mw-redirect" title="Inca civilization">Inca civilization</a> dominated the Andes region from 1438 to 1533. Known as <i>Tawantin suyu</i>, and "the land of the four regions," in <a href="/wiki/Quechua_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Quechua languages">Quechua</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">Inca Empire</a> was highly distinct and developed. Inca rule extended to nearly a hundred linguistic or ethnic communities, some nine to fourteen million people connected by a 25,000 kilometer <a href="/wiki/Inca_road_system" title="Inca road system">road system</a>. Cities were built with precise, unmatched stonework, constructed over many levels of mountain terrain. <a href="/wiki/Terrace_farming" class="mw-redirect" title="Terrace farming">Terrace farming</a> was a useful form of agriculture.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Mapuche" title="Mapuche">Mapuche</a> in Central and Southern Chile resisted the European and Chilean settlers, waging the <a href="/wiki/Arauco_War" title="Arauco War">Arauco War</a> for more than 300 years.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_colonization">European colonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: European colonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish colonization of the Americas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Portuguese colonization of the Americas">Portuguese colonization of the Americas</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vespucci%27s_first_voyage,_from_Letter_to_Soderini.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Vespucci%27s_first_voyage%2C_from_Letter_to_Soderini.jpg/220px-Vespucci%27s_first_voyage%2C_from_Letter_to_Soderini.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Vespucci%27s_first_voyage%2C_from_Letter_to_Soderini.jpg/330px-Vespucci%27s_first_voyage%2C_from_Letter_to_Soderini.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Vespucci%27s_first_voyage%2C_from_Letter_to_Soderini.jpg/440px-Vespucci%27s_first_voyage%2C_from_Letter_to_Soderini.jpg 2x" data-file-width="529" data-file-height="550" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vespucci%27s_first_voyage,_from_Letter_to_Soderini.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Woodcut depicting Italian explorer <a href="/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci" title="Amerigo Vespucci">Amerigo Vespucci</a>'s first voyage (1497-98) to the New World, from the first known published edition of Vespucci's 1504 letter to <a href="/wiki/Piero_Soderini" title="Piero Soderini">Piero Soderini</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In 1494, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, the two great maritime European powers of that time, on the expectation of new lands being discovered in the west, signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">Treaty of Tordesillas</a>, by which they agreed, with the support of the Pope, that all the land outside Europe should be an exclusive <a href="/wiki/Duopoly" title="Duopoly">duopoly</a> between the two countries.
</p><p>The treaty established an imaginary line along a north-south <a href="/wiki/Meridian_(geography)" title="Meridian (geography)">meridian</a> 370 <a href="/wiki/League_(unit)" title="League (unit)">leagues</a> west of the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape Verde Islands">Cape Verde Islands</a>, roughly 46° 37' W. In terms of the treaty, all land to the west of the line (known to comprise most of the South American soil) would belong to Spain, and all land to the east, to Portugal. As accurate measurements of <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">longitude</a> were impossible at that time, the line was not strictly enforced, resulting in a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Portuguese colonization of the Americas">Portuguese expansion of Brazil</a> across the meridian.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Inca-Spanish_confrontation.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Inca-Spanish_confrontation.JPG/220px-Inca-Spanish_confrontation.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Inca-Spanish_confrontation.JPG/330px-Inca-Spanish_confrontation.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Inca-Spanish_confrontation.JPG/440px-Inca-Spanish_confrontation.JPG 2x" data-file-width="968" data-file-height="733" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Inca-Spanish_confrontation.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Inca_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish conquest of the Inca Empire">Inca–Spanish confrontation</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cajamarca" title="Battle of Cajamarca">Battle of Cajamarca</a> left thousands of natives dead.</div></div></div>
<p>Beginning in the 1530s, the people and natural resources of South America were repeatedly exploited by foreign <a href="/wiki/Conquistadors" class="mw-redirect" title="Conquistadors">conquistadors</a>, first from Spain and later from Portugal. These competing colonial nations claimed the land and resources as their own and divided it in colonies.
</p><p>European infectious diseases (<a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Influenza" title="Influenza">influenza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Typhus" title="Typhus">typhus</a>) – to which the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">native populations</a> had no immune resistance&#160;– caused large-scale depopulation of the native population under Spanish control. Systems of forced labor, such as the <a href="/wiki/Hacienda" title="Hacienda">haciendas</a> and mining industry's <a href="/wiki/Mita_(Inca)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mita (Inca)">mit'a</a> also contributed to the depopulation. After this, African <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slaves</a>, who had developed immunities to these diseases, were quickly brought in to replace them.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_(1865%E2%80%931939).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_%281865%E2%80%931939%29.jpg/220px-Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_%281865%E2%80%931939%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_%281865%E2%80%931939%29.jpg/330px-Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_%281865%E2%80%931939%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_%281865%E2%80%931939%29.jpg/440px-Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_%281865%E2%80%931939%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2775" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_(1865%E2%80%931939).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Portuguese arrival in Brazil on 22 April 1500 was led by <a href="/wiki/Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral" title="Pedro Álvares Cabral">Pedro Álvares Cabral</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Waterkant_seen_from_Suriname_river_III.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Waterkant_seen_from_Suriname_river_III.JPG/220px-Waterkant_seen_from_Suriname_river_III.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Waterkant_seen_from_Suriname_river_III.JPG/330px-Waterkant_seen_from_Suriname_river_III.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Waterkant_seen_from_Suriname_river_III.JPG/440px-Waterkant_seen_from_Suriname_river_III.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Waterkant_seen_from_Suriname_river_III.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Dutch colonial houses in the historic center of <a href="/wiki/Paramaribo" title="Paramaribo">Paramaribo</a>, Suriname.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plate_6_Provisional_Battalion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Plate_6_Provisional_Battalion.jpg/220px-Plate_6_Provisional_Battalion.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Plate_6_Provisional_Battalion.jpg/330px-Plate_6_Provisional_Battalion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Plate_6_Provisional_Battalion.jpg/440px-Plate_6_Provisional_Battalion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="879" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plate_6_Provisional_Battalion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Illustration of the Demerara rebellion in <a href="/wiki/British_Guiana" title="British Guiana">British Guiana</a> in 1823.</div></div></div>
<p>The Spaniards were committed to converting their native subjects to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> and were quick to purge any native cultural practices that hindered this end; however, many initial attempts at this were only partially successful, as native groups simply blended <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicism">Catholicism</a> with their established beliefs and practices. Furthermore, the Spaniards brought their language to the degree they did with their religion, although the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>'s evangelization in <a href="/wiki/Quechua_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Quechua language">Quechua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Guaraní language">Guaraní</a> actually contributed to the continuous use of these native languages albeit only in the oral form.
</p><p>Eventually, the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">natives</a> and the Spaniards interbred, forming a <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizo</a> class. At the beginning, many mestizos of the Andean region were offspring of Amerindian mothers and Spanish fathers. After independence, most mestizos had native fathers and European or mestizo mothers.
</p><p>Many native artworks were considered pagan idols and destroyed by Spanish explorers; this included many gold and silver sculptures and other artifacts found in South America, which were melted down before their transport to Spain or Portugal. Spaniards and Portuguese brought the western European architectural style to the continent, and helped to improve infrastructures like bridges, roads, and the sewer system of the cities they discovered or conquered. They also significantly increased economic and trade relations, not just between the old and new world but between the different South American regions and peoples. Finally, with the expansion of the Portuguese and Spanish languages, many cultures that were previously separated became united through that of Latin American.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> was first a Dutch, and then a <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British colony</a>, though there was a brief period during the Napoleonic Wars when it was colonized by the French. The country was once partitioned into three parts, each being controlled by one of the colonial powers until the country was finally taken over fully by the British.
</p>
