</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Slavery" title="Template:Slavery"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Slavery" title="Template talk:Slavery"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Slavery&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Slavery_among_the_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Slavery among the indigenous peoples of the Americas">Slavery among the indigenous peoples of the Americas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Johann_Moritz_Rugendas_in_Brazil.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Johann_Moritz_Rugendas_in_Brazil.jpg/220px-Johann_Moritz_Rugendas_in_Brazil.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Johann_Moritz_Rugendas_in_Brazil.jpg/330px-Johann_Moritz_Rugendas_in_Brazil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Johann_Moritz_Rugendas_in_Brazil.jpg/440px-Johann_Moritz_Rugendas_in_Brazil.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4569" data-file-height="3359" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Johann_Moritz_Rugendas_in_Brazil.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Public flogging of a slave in 19th-century Brazil.</div></div></div>
<p>Indigenous peoples of the Americas in various European colonies were forced to work in European plantations and mines; along with African slaves who were also introduced in the proceeding centuries. The colonists were heavily dependent on indigenous labor during the initial phases of European settlement to maintain the subsistence economy, and natives were often captured by expeditions. The importation of African slaves began midway through the 16th century, but the enslavement of indigenous peoples continued well into the 17th and 18th centuries. The <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a> brought African slaves primarily to South American colonies, beginning with the Portuguese since 1502.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The main destinations of this phase were the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> colonies and <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, as European nations built up economically slave-dependent colonies in the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>. Nearly 40% of all African slaves trafficked to the Americas went to Brazil. An estimated 4.9 million slaves from Africa came to Brazil during the period from 1501 to 1866.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While the Portuguese, English and French settlers enslaved mainly African blacks, the Spaniards became very disposed of the natives. In 1750 Portugal abolished native slavery in the colonies because they considered them unfit for labour and began to import even more African slaves. Slaves were brought to the mainland on so-called <a href="/wiki/Slave_ships" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave ships">slave ships</a>, under inhuman conditions and ill-treatment, and those who survived were sold into the slave markets.
</p><p>After independence, all South American countries maintained slavery for some time. The first South American country to abolish slavery was Chile in 1823, Uruguay in 1830, Bolivia in 1831, Colombia and Ecuador in 1851, Argentina in 1853, Peru and Venezuela in 1854, Paraguay in 1869, and in 1888 Brazil was the last South American nation and the last country in <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">western world</a> to abolish slavery.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_from_Spain_and_Portugal">Independence from Spain and Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Independence from Spain and Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">Spanish American wars of independence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil" title="Independence of Brazil">Independence of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg/220px-Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg/330px-Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg/440px-Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg 2x" data-file-width="577" data-file-height="543" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil_conference" class="mw-redirect" title="Guayaquil conference">Guayaquil conference</a> between <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_San_Mart%C3%ADn" title="José de San Martín">José de San Martín</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_(1888).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_%281888%29.jpg/220px-Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_%281888%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_%281888%29.jpg/330px-Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_%281888%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_%281888%29.jpg/440px-Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_%281888%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2271" data-file-height="1268" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_(1888).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The proclamation of the <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil" title="Independence of Brazil">Independence of Brazil</a> by <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Prince Pedro</a> on 7 September 1822</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coroa%C3%A7ao_pedro_I_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Coroa%C3%A7ao_pedro_I_001.jpg/220px-Coroa%C3%A7ao_pedro_I_001.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Coroa%C3%A7ao_pedro_I_001.jpg/330px-Coroa%C3%A7ao_pedro_I_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Coroa%C3%A7ao_pedro_I_001.jpg/440px-Coroa%C3%A7ao_pedro_I_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2718" data-file-height="1586" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coroa%C3%A7ao_pedro_I_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coronation of <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Pedro I</a> as 1st <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Emperor of Brazil">Emperor of Brazil</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JuraIndependencia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/JuraIndependencia.jpg/220px-JuraIndependencia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/JuraIndependencia.jpg/330px-JuraIndependencia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/JuraIndependencia.jpg/440px-JuraIndependencia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1077" data-file-height="709" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JuraIndependencia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bernardo_O%27Higgins" title="Bernardo O&#39;Higgins">Bernardo O'Higgins</a> swears officially the independence of <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The European <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a> (1807–1814), a theater of the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, changed the political situation of both the Spanish and Portuguese colonies. First, Napoleon invaded Portugal, but the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Braganza" title="House of Braganza">House of Braganza</a> avoided capture by <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_the_Portuguese_Court_to_Brazil" title="Transfer of the Portuguese Court to Brazil">escaping to Brazil</a>. Napoleon also captured King <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">Ferdinand VII of Spain</a>, and appointed his own brother instead. This appointment provoked severe popular resistance, which created <a href="/wiki/Junta_(Peninsular_War)" title="Junta (Peninsular War)">Juntas</a> to rule in the name of the captured king.
</p><p>Many cities in the Spanish colonies, however, considered themselves equally authorized to appoint local Juntas like those of Spain. This began the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">Spanish American wars of independence</a> between the patriots, who promoted such autonomy, and the <a href="/wiki/Royalist_(Spanish_American_Revolution)" class="mw-redirect" title="Royalist (Spanish American Revolution)">royalists</a>, who supported Spanish authority over the Americas. The Juntas, in both Spain and the Americas, promoted the ideas of the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a>. Five years after the beginning of the war, Ferdinand VII returned to the throne and began the <a href="/wiki/Absolutist_Restoration" class="mw-redirect" title="Absolutist Restoration">Absolutist Restoration</a> as the royalists got the upper hand in the conflict.
</p><p>The independence of South America was secured by <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a> (Venezuela) and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_San_Mart%C3%ADn" title="José de San Martín">José de San Martín</a> (Argentina), the two most important <i><a href="/wiki/Libertadores" title="Libertadores">Libertadores</a></i>. Bolívar led a great uprising in the north, then led his army southward towards <a href="/wiki/Lima" title="Lima">Lima</a>, the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_Peru" title="Viceroyalty of Peru">Viceroyalty of Peru</a>. Meanwhile, San Martín led an army across the Andes Mountains, along with Chilean expatriates, and liberated Chile. He organized a fleet to reach Peru by sea, and sought the military support of various rebels from the Viceroyalty of Peru. The two armies finally met in Guayaquil, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, where they cornered the Royal Army of the Spanish Crown and forced its surrender.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Portugal,_Brazil_and_the_Algarves" title="United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves">Portuguese Kingdom of Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dom_Pedro_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Dom Pedro I">Dom Pedro I</a> (also Pedro IV of Portugal), son of the Portuguese King <a href="/wiki/Dom_Jo%C3%A3o_VI" class="mw-redirect" title="Dom João VI">Dom João VI</a>, proclaimed the independent <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Brazil" title="Kingdom of Brazil">Kingdom of Brazil</a> in 1822, which later became the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a>. Despite the Portuguese loyalties of garrisons in <a href="/wiki/Bahia" title="Bahia">Bahia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cisplatine_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Cisplatine Province">Cisplatina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Par%C3%A1" title="Pará">Pará</a>, independence was diplomatically accepted by the crown in Portugal in 1825, on condition of a high compensation paid by Brazil mediatized by the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nation-building_and_fragmentation">Nation-building and fragmentation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Nation-building and fragmentation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Juan_Manuel_Blanes_-_El_Juramento_de_los_Treinta_y_Tres_Orientales.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Juan_Manuel_Blanes_-_El_Juramento_de_los_Treinta_y_Tres_Orientales.jpg/220px-Juan_Manuel_Blanes_-_El_Juramento_de_los_Treinta_y_Tres_Orientales.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Juan_Manuel_Blanes_-_El_Juramento_de_los_Treinta_y_Tres_Orientales.jpg/330px-Juan_Manuel_Blanes_-_El_Juramento_de_los_Treinta_y_Tres_Orientales.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Juan_Manuel_Blanes_-_El_Juramento_de_los_Treinta_y_Tres_Orientales.jpg/440px-Juan_Manuel_Blanes_-_El_Juramento_de_los_Treinta_y_Tres_Orientales.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2088" data-file-height="1115" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Juan_Manuel_Blanes_-_El_Juramento_de_los_Treinta_y_Tres_Orientales.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Thirty-Three_Orientals" title="Thirty-Three Orientals">Thirty-Three Orientals</a> proclaimed the independence of <a href="/wiki/Cisplatine_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Cisplatine Province">Cisplatine Province</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_-_Cena_de_Batalha_no_Sul_do_Brasil.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_-_Cena_de_Batalha_no_Sul_do_Brasil.jpg/220px-Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_-_Cena_de_Batalha_no_Sul_do_Brasil.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_-_Cena_de_Batalha_no_Sul_do_Brasil.jpg/330px-Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_-_Cena_de_Batalha_no_Sul_do_Brasil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9c/Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_-_Cena_de_Batalha_no_Sul_do_Brasil.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="297" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_-_Cena_de_Batalha_no_Sul_do_Brasil.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Battle of Fanfa, battle scene in Southern Brazil during the <a href="/wiki/Ragamuffin_War" title="Ragamuffin War">Ragamuffin War</a></div></div></div>
<p>The newly independent nations began a process of fragmentation, with several civil and international wars. However, it was not as strong as in Central America. Some countries created from provinces of larger countries stayed as such up to modern times (such as Paraguay or Uruguay), while others were reconquered and reincorporated into their former countries (such as the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Entre_R%C3%ADos" title="Republic of Entre Ríos">Republic of Entre Ríos</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Riograndense_Republic" title="Riograndense Republic">Riograndense Republic</a>).
</p><p>The first separatist attempt was in 1820 by the Argentine province of <a href="/wiki/Entre_R%C3%ADos_Province" title="Entre Ríos Province">Entre Ríos</a>, led by a <a href="/wiki/Caudillo" title="Caudillo">caudillo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In spite of the "Republic" in its title, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Ram%C3%ADrez_(governor)" title="Francisco Ramírez (governor)">General Ramírez</a>, its caudillo, never really intended to declare an independent Entre Rios. Rather, he was making a political statement in opposition to the monarchist and centralist ideas that back then permeated <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a> politics. The "country" was reincorporated at the United Provinces in 1821.
</p><p>In 1825 the <a href="/wiki/Cisplatine_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Cisplatine Province">Cisplatine Province</a> declared its independence from the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a>, which led to the <a href="/wiki/Cisplatine_War" title="Cisplatine War">Cisplatine War</a> between the imperials and the Argentine from the <a href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_the_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" class="mw-redirect" title="United Provinces of the Río de la Plata">United Provinces of the Río de la Plata</a> to control the region. Three years later, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> intervened in the question by proclaiming a tie and creating in the former Cisplatina a new independent country: The <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Republic_of_Uruguay" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental Republic of Uruguay">Oriental Republic of Uruguay</a>.
</p><p>Later in 1836, while Brazil was experiencing the chaos of the regency, <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">Rio Grande do Sul</a> <a href="/wiki/Ragamuffin_War" title="Ragamuffin War">proclaimed its independence</a> motivated by a tax crisis. With the anticipation of the coronation of <a href="/wiki/Pedro_II_of_Brazil" title="Pedro II of Brazil">Pedro II</a> to the throne of Brazil, the country could stabilize and fight the separatists, which the province of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_(state)" title="Santa Catarina (state)">Santa Catarina</a> had joined in 1839. The Conflict came to an end by a process of compromise by which both <a href="/wiki/Riograndense_Republic" title="Riograndense Republic">Riograndense Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juliana_Republic" title="Juliana Republic">Juliana Republic</a> were reincorporated as provinces in 1845.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Peru%E2%80%93Bolivian_Confederation" title="Peru–Bolivian Confederation">Peru–Bolivian Confederation</a>, a short-lived union of Peru and Bolivia, was blocked by Chile in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Confederation" title="War of the Confederation">War of the Confederation</a> (1836–1839) and again during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a> (1879–1883). Paraguay was virtually destroyed by Argentina, Brazil and Uruguay in the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wars_and_conflicts">Wars and conflicts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Wars and conflicts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brazilians_during_the_siege_of_Paysandu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Brazilians_during_the_siege_of_Paysandu.jpg/220px-Brazilians_during_the_siege_of_Paysandu.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Brazilians_during_the_siege_of_Paysandu.jpg/330px-Brazilians_during_the_siege_of_Paysandu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Brazilians_during_the_siege_of_Paysandu.jpg/440px-Brazilians_during_the_siege_of_Paysandu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2128" data-file-height="1286" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brazilians_during_the_siege_of_Paysandu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Imperial_Brazilian_Navy" title="Imperial Brazilian Navy">Imperial Brazilian Navy</a> and army troops during the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Paysand%C3%BA" title="Siege of Paysandú">Siege of Paysandú</a>, 1865</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Potrero_Sauce_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Battle_of_Potrero_Sauce_01.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Potrero_Sauce_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Battle_of_Potrero_Sauce_01.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Potrero_Sauce_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Battle_of_Potrero_Sauce_01.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Potrero_Sauce_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1237" data-file-height="808" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Potrero_Sauce_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Uruguayan_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Uruguayan Army">Uruguayan Army</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sauce" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Sauce">Battle of Sauce</a>, 1866</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Procession_in_Paraguay_1868.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Procession_in_Paraguay_1868.jpg/220px-Procession_in_Paraguay_1868.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Procession_in_Paraguay_1868.jpg/330px-Procession_in_Paraguay_1868.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Procession_in_Paraguay_1868.jpg/440px-Procession_in_Paraguay_1868.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1372" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Procession_in_Paraguay_1868.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Brazilian_Army" title="Imperial Brazilian Army">Imperial Brazilian Army</a> during a procession in <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a>, 1868</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Batalla_de_Chorrillos.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Batalla_de_Chorrillos.jpg/220px-Batalla_de_Chorrillos.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Batalla_de_Chorrillos.jpg/330px-Batalla_de_Chorrillos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Batalla_de_Chorrillos.jpg/440px-Batalla_de_Chorrillos.jpg 2x" data-file-width="999" data-file-height="784" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Batalla_de_Chorrillos.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Army" title="Chilean Army">Chilean Army</a> in the battlefield of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chorrillos" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Chorrillos">Battle of Chorrillos</a>, 1883</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U-199Flyover.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/U-199Flyover.jpg/220px-U-199Flyover.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/U-199Flyover.jpg/330px-U-199Flyover.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/U-199Flyover.jpg/440px-U-199Flyover.jpg 2x" data-file-width="668" data-file-height="520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:U-199Flyover.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A German submarine under attack by <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Air_Force" title="Brazilian Air Force">Brazilian Air Force</a> PBY Catalina, 31<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>July 1943</div></div></div>
<p>South American history in early <a href="/wiki/19th_century" title="19th century">19th century</a> was built almost exclusively on wars. Despite the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">Spanish American wars of independence</a> and the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Independence_of_Brazil" title="War of Independence of Brazil">Brazilian War of Independence</a>, the new nations quickly began to suffer with internal conflicts and wars among themselves.
</p><p>In 1825 the proclamation of independence of Cisplatina led to the <a href="/wiki/Cisplatine_War" title="Cisplatine War">Cisplatine War</a> between historical rivals the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_the_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" class="mw-redirect" title="United Provinces of the Río de la Plata">United Provinces of the Río de la Plata</a>, Argentina's predecessor. The result was a stalemate, ending with the British arranging for the independence of Uruguay. Soon after, another Brazilian province proclaimed its independence leading to the <a href="/wiki/Ragamuffin_War" title="Ragamuffin War">Ragamuffin War</a> which Brazil won.
</p><p>Between 1836 and 1839 the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Confederation" title="War of the Confederation">War of the Confederation</a> broke out between the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Peru-Bolivian_Confederation" class="mw-redirect" title="Peru-Bolivian Confederation">Peru-Bolivian Confederation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, with the support of the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Confederation" title="Argentine Confederation">Argentine Confederation</a>. The war was fought mostly in the actual territory of <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> and ended with a Confederate defeat and the dissolution of the Confederacy and annexation of many territories by Argentina.
</p><p>Meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Civil_Wars" title="Argentine Civil Wars">Argentine Civil Wars</a> plagued Argentina since its independence. The conflict was mainly between those who defended the centralization of power in Buenos Aires and those who defended a confederation. During this period it can be said that "there were two Argentines": the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Confederation" title="Argentine Confederation">Argentine Confederation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Argentine Republic">Argentine Republic</a>. At the same time the political instability in Uruguay led to the <a href="/wiki/Uruguayan_Civil_War" title="Uruguayan Civil War">Uruguayan Civil War</a> among the main political factions of the country. All this instability in the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata_Basin" title="Río de la Plata Basin">platine region</a> interfered with the goals of other countries such as Brazil, which was soon forced to take sides. In 1851 the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian Empire">Brazilian Empire</a>, supporting the centralizing unitarians, and the <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguayan government</a> invaded Argentina and deposed the caudillo, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Rosas" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan Manuel Rosas">Juan Manuel Rosas</a>, who ruled the confederation with an iron hand. Although the <a href="/wiki/Platine_War" title="Platine War">Platine War</a> did not put an end to the political chaos and civil war in Argentina, it brought temporary peace to Uruguay where the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Party_(Uruguay)" title="Colorado Party (Uruguay)">Colorados faction</a> won, supported by the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian Empire">Brazilian Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Second_French_Empire" title="Second French Empire">French Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Unitarian_Party" title="Unitarian Party">Unitarian Party</a> of Argentina.<sup id="cite_ref-Latin_America’s_Wars_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Latin_America’s_Wars-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Peace lasted only a short time: in 1864 the Uruguayan factions faced each other again in the <a href="/wiki/Uruguayan_War" title="Uruguayan War">Uruguayan War</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_Party_(Uruguay)" title="National Party (Uruguay)">Blancos</a> supported by Paraguay started to attack Brazilian and Argentine farmers near the borders. The Empire made an initial attempt to settle the dispute between Blancos and Colorados without success. In 1864, after a Brazilian ultimatum was refused, the imperial government declared that Brazil's military would begin reprisals. Brazil declined to acknowledge a formal state of war, and, for most of its duration, the Uruguayan–Brazilian armed conflict was an undeclared war which led to the deposition of the <i>Blancos</i> and the rise of the pro-Brazilian <i>Colorados</i> to power again. This angered the Paraguayan government, which even before the end of the war invaded Brazil, beginning the biggest and deadliest war in both South American and Latin American histories: the Paraguayan War.
</p><p>The Paraguayan War began when the Paraguayan dictator <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Solano_L%C3%B3pez" title="Francisco Solano López">Francisco Solano López</a> ordered the invasion of the Brazilian provinces of <a href="/wiki/Mato_Grosso" title="Mato Grosso">Mato Grosso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">Rio Grande do Sul</a>. His attempt to cross Argentinian territory without Argentinian approval led the pro-Brazilian Argentine government into the war. The pro-Brazilian Uruguayan government showed its support by sending troops. In 1865 the three countries signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_the_Triple_Alliance" title="Treaty of the Triple Alliance">Treaty of the Triple Alliance</a> against Paraguay. At the beginning of the war, the Paraguayans took the lead with several victories, until the Triple Alliance organized to repel the invaders and fight effectively. This was the second <a href="/wiki/Total_war" title="Total war">total war</a> experience in the world after the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>. It was deemed the greatest war effort in the history of all participating countries, taking almost 6 years and ending with the complete devastation of Paraguay. The country lost 40% of its territory to Brazil and Argentina and lost 60% of its population, including 90% of the men. The dictator Lopez was killed in battle and a new government was instituted in alliance with Brazil, which maintained occupation forces in the country until 1876.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The last South American war in the 19th century was the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a> with Bolivia and Peru on one side and Chile on the other. In 1879 the war began with Chilean troops occupying Bolivian ports, followed by Bolivia declaring war on Chile which activated an alliance treaty with Peru. The Bolivians were completely defeated in 1880 and Lima was occupied in 1881. The peace was signed with Peru in 1883 while a truce was signed with Bolivia in 1884. Chile annexed territories of both countries leaving Bolivia with no path to the sea.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the new century, as wars became less violent and less frequent, Brazil entered into a small conflict with Bolivia for the possession of the Acre, which was acquired by Brazil in 1902. In 1917 Brazil declared war on the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> and join the allied side in the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, sending a small fleet to the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> and some troops to be integrated with the British and French troops. Brazil was the only South American country that fought in WWI.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Later in 1932 Colombia and Peru entered a <a href="/wiki/Leticia_Incident" title="Leticia Incident">short armed conflict</a> for territory in the Amazon. In the same year Paraguay declared <a href="/wiki/Chaco_War" title="Chaco War">war</a> on Bolivia for possession of the Chaco, in a conflict that ended three years later with Paraguay's victory. Between 1941 and 1942 Peru and Ecuador <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian%E2%80%93Peruvian_War" title="Ecuadorian–Peruvian War">fought decisively for territories</a> claimed by both that were annexed by Peru, usurping Ecuador's frontier with Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Also in this period the first naval battle of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> was fought on the continent, in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_River_Plate" title="Battle of the River Plate">River Plate</a>, between British forces and German submarines.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The Germans still made numerous attacks on Brazilian ships on the coast, causing Brazil to declare war on the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a> in 1942, being the only South American country to fight in this war (and in both World Wars). Brazil sent naval and air forces to <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic" title="Battle of the Atlantic">combat German and Italian submarines</a> off the continent and throughout the South Atlantic, in addition to sending an <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Expeditionary_Force" title="Brazilian Expeditionary Force">expeditionary force</a> to fight in the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Campaign_(World_War_II)" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Campaign (World War II)">Italian Campaign</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ibidem_Maximiano_2011_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ibidem_Maximiano_2011-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ibidem_Maximiano_2011_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ibidem_Maximiano_2011-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A brief war was fought between Argentina and the UK in 1982, following an Argentine invasion of the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a>, which ended with an Argentine defeat. The last international war to be fought on South American soil was the 1995 <a href="/wiki/Cenepa_War" title="Cenepa War">Cenepa War</a> between Ecuador and the Peru along their mutual border.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_and_fall_of_military_dictatorships">Rise and fall of military dictatorships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Rise and fall of military dictatorships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Soldadosargentinos3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Soldadosargentinos3.jpg/220px-Soldadosargentinos3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="268" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Soldadosargentinos3.jpg/330px-Soldadosargentinos3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Soldadosargentinos3.jpg/440px-Soldadosargentinos3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1343" data-file-height="1638" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Soldadosargentinos3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Argentine soldiers during the <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg/220px-Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg/330px-Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg/440px-Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1857" data-file-height="1332" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Minas_Geraes-class_battleship" title="Minas Geraes-class battleship"><i>Minas Geraes</i> class</a> kindled an <a href="/wiki/South_American_dreadnought_race" title="South American dreadnought race">Argentine–Brazilian–Chilean naval arms race</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Wars became less frequent in the 20th century, with Bolivia-Paraguay and Peru-Ecuador fighting the last inter-state wars. Early in the 20th century, the <a href="/wiki/ABC_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="ABC Powers">three wealthiest South American countries</a> engaged in <a href="/wiki/South_American_dreadnought_race" title="South American dreadnought race">a vastly expensive naval arms race</a> which was catalyzed by the introduction of a new warship type, the "<a href="/wiki/Dreadnought" title="Dreadnought">dreadnought</a>". At one point, the Argentine government was spending a fifth of its entire yearly budget for just two dreadnoughts, a price that did not include later in-service costs, which for the Brazilian dreadnoughts was sixty percent of the initial purchase.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The continent became a battlefield of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> in the late 20th century. Some democratically elected governments of Argentina, Brazil, Chile, Uruguay and Paraguay were overthrown or displaced by military dictatorships in the 1960s and 1970s. To curtail opposition, their governments detained tens of thousands of <a href="/wiki/Political_prisoner" title="Political prisoner">political prisoners</a>, many of whom were tortured and/or killed on <a href="/wiki/Operation_Condor" title="Operation Condor">inter-state collaboration</a>. Economically, they began a transition to <a href="/wiki/Neoliberal" class="mw-redirect" title="Neoliberal">neoliberal</a> economic policies. They placed their own actions within the US Cold War doctrine of "National Security" against internal subversion. Throughout the 1980s and 1990s, Peru suffered from <a href="/wiki/Internal_conflict_in_Peru" title="Internal conflict in Peru">an internal conflict</a>.
</p><p>Argentina and Britain fought the <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a> in 1982.
</p><p>Colombia has had an ongoing, though diminished internal conflict, which started in 1964 with the creation of <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxist</a> <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrillas</a> (FARC-EP) and then involved several illegal armed groups of leftist-leaning ideology as well as the private armies of powerful drug lords. Many of these are now defunct, and only a small portion of the ELN remains, along with the stronger, though also greatly reduced, FARC. These leftist groups smuggle narcotics out of Colombia to fund their operations, while also using kidnapping, bombings, land mines and assassinations as weapons against both elected and non-elected citizens.
</p><p>Revolutionary movements and right-wing military dictatorships became common after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, but since the 1980s, a wave of democratization passed through the continent, and democratic rule is widespread now.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, allegations of corruption are still very common, and several countries have developed crises which have forced the resignation of their governments, although, on most occasions, regular civilian succession has continued.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Presidentes_unasur_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Presidentes_unasur_%28cropped%29.jpg/240px-Presidentes_unasur_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="240" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Presidentes_unasur_%28cropped%29.jpg/360px-Presidentes_unasur_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Presidentes_unasur_%28cropped%29.jpg/480px-Presidentes_unasur_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2480" data-file-height="1002" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Presidentes_unasur_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Presidents of <a href="/wiki/UNASUR" class="mw-redirect" title="UNASUR">UNASUR</a> member states at the Second Brasília Summit on 23 May 2008.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Developing_countries%27_debt" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing countries&#39; debt">International indebtedness</a> turned into a severe problem in the late 1980s, and some countries, despite having strong democracies, have not yet developed political institutions capable of handling such crises without resorting to unorthodox economic policies, as most recently illustrated by Argentina's <a href="/wiki/Argentine_economic_crisis_(1999-2002)" class="mw-redirect" title="Argentine economic crisis (1999-2002)">default</a> in the early 21st century.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view"><span title="This statement is possibly biased. (November 2012)">neutrality</span></a>&#32;is <a href="/wiki/Talk:South_America" title="Talk:South America">disputed</a></i>&#93;</sup> The last twenty years have seen an increased push towards <a href="/wiki/Integration_of_Latin_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Integration of Latin America">regional integration</a>, with the creation of uniquely South American institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/Andean_Community" title="Andean Community">Andean Community</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unasur" class="mw-redirect" title="Unasur">Unasur</a>. Notably, starting with the election of <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">Hugo Chávez</a> in Venezuela in 1998, the region experienced what has been termed a <a href="/wiki/Pink_tide" title="Pink tide">pink tide</a> – the election of several leftist and center-left administrations to most countries of the area, except for the Guianas and Colombia.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_and_territories">Countries and territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Countries and territories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_South_American_countries_by_population" title="List of South American countries by population">List of South American countries by population</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_South_America_by_median_age_of_population" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories in South America by median age of population">List of sovereign states and dependent territories in South America by median age of population</a></div>

</th>
<th class="unsortable">Flag

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UNASUR_(Ecuador).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/UNASUR_%28Ecuador%29.jpg/220px-UNASUR_%28Ecuador%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/UNASUR_%28Ecuador%29.jpg/330px-UNASUR_%28Ecuador%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/UNASUR_%28Ecuador%29.jpg/440px-UNASUR_%28Ecuador%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UNASUR_(Ecuador).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/UNASUR" class="mw-redirect" title="UNASUR">UNASUR</a> in <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SACN_member_states.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/SACN_member_states.jpg/220px-SACN_member_states.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="320" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/SACN_member_states.jpg/330px-SACN_member_states.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/08/SACN_member_states.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="581" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SACN_member_states.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_geoscheme" title="United Nations geoscheme">Scheme for geographic regions and subregions</a> used by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Statistics_Division" title="United Nations Statistics Division">United Nations Statistics Division</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg/220px-Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg/330px-Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg/440px-Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>South American flags</div></div></div>
<p>Historically, the Hispanic countries were founded as Republican dictatorships led by <a href="/wiki/Caudillo" title="Caudillo">caudillos</a>. <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> was the only exception, being a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> for its first 67 years of independence, until a <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d&#39;état">coup d'état</a> proclaimed a republic. In the late 19th century, the most democratic countries were <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Brazil</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELira_1977,_Vol_29_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELira_1977,_Vol_29-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed (May 2019)">full citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/History_of_Chile_during_the_Parliamentary_Era_(1891%E2%80%931925)" title="History of Chile during the Parliamentary Era (1891–1925)">Chile</a>, Argentina and Uruguay.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the interwar period, nationalism grew stronger on the continent, influenced by countries like <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Social_Republic" title="Italian Social Republic">Fascist Italy</a>. A series of authoritarian rules broke out in South American countries with views bringing them closer to the <a href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis Powers">Axis Powers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> like <a href="/wiki/Vargas_Era" title="Vargas Era">Vargas's Brazil</a>. In the late 20th century, during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, many countries became <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorships" class="mw-redirect" title="Military dictatorships">military dictatorships</a> under American tutelage in attempts to avoid the influence of the Soviet Union. After the fall of the authoritarian regimes, these countries became democratic republics.
</p><p>During the first decade of the 21st century, South American governments have drifted to the political left, with leftist leaders being elected in Chile, Uruguay, Brazil, Argentina, Ecuador, Bolivia, Paraguay, Peru and Venezuela. Most South American countries are making increasing use of protectionist policies, helping local development.
</p><p>All South American countries are <a href="/wiki/Presidential_republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Presidential republic">presidential republics</a> with the exceptions of Peru, which is a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-presidential republic">semi-presidential republic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a>. <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> is a <a href="/wiki/French_overseas_department" class="mw-redirect" title="French overseas department">French overseas department</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands</a> are British overseas territories. It is currently the only inhabited continent in the world without <a href="/wiki/Monarchies" class="mw-redirect" title="Monarchies">monarchies</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a> existed during the 19th century and there was an unsuccessful attempt to establish a <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Araucan%C3%ADa_and_Patagonia" title="Kingdom of Araucanía and Patagonia">Kingdom of Araucanía and Patagonia</a> in southern Argentina and Chile. Also in the twentieth century, <a href="/wiki/Suriname_(Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands)" title="Suriname (Kingdom of the Netherlands)">Suriname</a> was established as a constituent kingdom of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guyana_(1966%E2%80%931970)" title="Guyana (1966–1970)">Guyana</a> retained the <a href="/wiki/British_monarch" class="mw-redirect" title="British monarch">British monarch</a> as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> for 4 years after its independence.
</p><p>Recently, an intergovernmental entity has been formed which aims to merge the two existing customs unions: <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Andean_Community" title="Andean Community">Andean Community</a>, thus forming the third-largest trade bloc in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
This new political organization, known as <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Union of South American Nations">Union of South American Nations</a>, seeks to establish free movement of people, economic development, a common defense policy and the elimination of <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariffs</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:South_America_night.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/South_America_night.jpg/220px-South_America_night.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="247" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/South_America_night.jpg/330px-South_America_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/South_America_night.jpg/440px-South_America_night.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2447" data-file-height="2750" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:South_America_night.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satellite view of South America at night from <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>South America has over 420 million<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> inhabitants and a population growth rate of about 0.6% per year. There are several areas of sparse demographics such as <a href="/wiki/Tropical_forest" title="Tropical forest">tropical forests</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Atacama_Desert" title="Atacama Desert">Atacama Desert</a> and the icy portions of <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">Patagonia</a>. On the other hand, the continent presents regions of high population density, such as the great urban centers. The population is formed by descendants of Europeans (mainly <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spaniards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italians</a>), <a href="/wiki/Africans" class="mw-redirect" title="Africans">Africans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous peoples</a>. There is a high percentage of <a href="/wiki/Mestizos" class="mw-redirect" title="Mestizos">mestizos</a> that vary greatly in composition by place. There is also a minor population of <a href="/wiki/Asians" class="mw-redirect" title="Asians">Asians</a>, especially in Brazil. The two main languages are by far Spanish and Portuguese, followed by French, English and Dutch in smaller numbers.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_South_America_(en).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Languages_of_South_America_%28en%29.svg/220px-Languages_of_South_America_%28en%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Languages_of_South_America_%28en%29.svg/330px-Languages_of_South_America_%28en%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Languages_of_South_America_%28en%29.svg/440px-Languages_of_South_America_%28en%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="402" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_South_America_(en).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Official languages in South America</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> are the most spoken languages in South America, with approximately 200 million speakers each. Spanish is the official language of most countries, along with other native languages in some countries. Portuguese is the official language of Brazil. <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> is the official language of <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>; <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is the official language of <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, although there are at least twelve other languages spoken in the country, including <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Hindustani" title="Caribbean Hindustani">Hindustani</a> and several native languages.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> English is also spoken in the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a>. <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> is the official language of <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> and the second language in <a href="/wiki/Amap%C3%A1" title="Amapá">Amapá</a>, Brazil.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">Indigenous languages</a> of South America include <a href="/wiki/Quechua_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Quechua languages">Quechua</a> in Peru, Bolivia, Ecuador, Argentina, Chile and Colombia; <a href="/wiki/Wayuunaiki" class="mw-redirect" title="Wayuunaiki">Wayuunaiki</a> in northern Colombia (<a href="/wiki/La_Guajira" class="mw-redirect" title="La Guajira">La Guajira</a>) and northwestern Venezuela (<a href="/wiki/Zulia" title="Zulia">Zulia</a>); <a href="/wiki/Guarani_language" title="Guarani language">Guaraní</a> in Paraguay and, to a much lesser extent, in Bolivia; <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a> in Bolivia, Peru, and less often in Chile; and <a href="/wiki/Mapudungun" class="mw-redirect" title="Mapudungun">Mapudungun</a> is spoken in certain pockets of southern Chile and, more rarely, Argentina. At least three South American indigenous languages (Quechua, Aymara, and Guarani) are recognized along with Spanish as national languages.
</p><p>Other languages found in South America include <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Hindustani" title="Caribbean Hindustani">Hindustani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Javanese_language" title="Javanese language">Javanese</a> in Suriname; <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> in Argentina, Brazil, Uruguay, Venezuela and Chile; and <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> in certain pockets of Argentina, Brazil, and Chile. German is also spoken in many regions of the southern states of Brazil, <a href="/wiki/Riograndenser_Hunsr%C3%BCckisch" class="mw-redirect" title="Riograndenser Hunsrückisch">Riograndenser Hunsrückisch</a> being the most widely spoken German dialect in the country; among other Germanic dialects, a Brazilian form of <a href="/wiki/East_Pomeranian_dialect" title="East Pomeranian dialect">East Pomeranian</a> is also well represented and is experiencing a revival. <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a> remains spoken and written in the historic towns of <a href="/wiki/Trelew" title="Trelew">Trelew</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rawson,_Chubut" title="Rawson, Chubut">Rawson</a> in the Argentine <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">Patagonia</a>. There are also small clusters of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>-speakers in Brazil, Colombia and Peru. Arabic speakers, often of <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">Lebanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syrian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian people">Syrian</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> descent, can be found in Arab communities in Argentina, Colombia, Brazil, Venezuela and in Paraguay.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Santuario_de_Las_Lajas,_Ipiales,_Colombia,_2015-07-21,_DD_21-23_HDR-Edit.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Santuario_de_Las_Lajas%2C_Ipiales%2C_Colombia%2C_2015-07-21%2C_DD_21-23_HDR-Edit.JPG/220px-Santuario_de_Las_Lajas%2C_Ipiales%2C_Colombia%2C_2015-07-21%2C_DD_21-23_HDR-Edit.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Santuario_de_Las_Lajas%2C_Ipiales%2C_Colombia%2C_2015-07-21%2C_DD_21-23_HDR-Edit.JPG/330px-Santuario_de_Las_Lajas%2C_Ipiales%2C_Colombia%2C_2015-07-21%2C_DD_21-23_HDR-Edit.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Santuario_de_Las_Lajas%2C_Ipiales%2C_Colombia%2C_2015-07-21%2C_DD_21-23_HDR-Edit.JPG/440px-Santuario_de_Las_Lajas%2C_Ipiales%2C_Colombia%2C_2015-07-21%2C_DD_21-23_HDR-Edit.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3958" data-file-height="2758" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Santuario_de_Las_Lajas,_Ipiales,_Colombia,_2015-07-21,_DD_21-23_HDR-Edit.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Las_Lajas_Sanctuary" title="Las Lajas Sanctuary">Las Lajas Sanctuary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ipiales" title="Ipiales">Ipiales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Latin_America" title="Religion in Latin America">Religion in Latin America</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Latin_America_and_the_Caribbean" title="History of the Jews in Latin America and the Caribbean">History of the Jews in Latin America and the Caribbean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Brazil" title="Buddhism in Brazil">Buddhism in Brazil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Argentina" title="Islam in Argentina">Islam in Argentina</a></div>
<p>An estimated 90% of South Americans are <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> (82% <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>, 8% other Christian denominations mainly traditional <a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelicals" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelicals">Evangelicals</a> but also <a href="/wiki/Orthodoxy" title="Orthodoxy">Orthodox</a>), accounting for c. 19% of Christians worldwide.
</p><p>African descendent religions and Indigenous religions are also common throughout all South America, some examples of are <a href="/wiki/Santo_Daime" title="Santo Daime">Santo Daime</a>, <a href="/wiki/Candombl%C3%A9" title="Candomblé">Candomblé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Umbanda" title="Umbanda">Umbanda</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Encantados&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Encantados (page does not exist)">Encantados</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Crypto-Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Crypto-Jews">Crypto-Jews</a> or <a href="/wiki/Marrano" title="Marrano">Marranos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conversos" class="mw-redirect" title="Conversos">conversos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anusim" title="Anusim">Anusim</a> were an important part of colonial life in Latin America.
</p><p>Both Buenos Aires, Argentina and São Paulo, Brazil figure among the largest <a href="/wiki/Jewish_population_by_urban_areas" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish population by urban areas">Jewish populations by urban area</a>.
</p><p>Japanese Buddhism, <a href="/wiki/Shintoism" class="mw-redirect" title="Shintoism">Shintoism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shinto" title="Shinto">Shinto-derived</a> <a href="/wiki/Japanese_New_Religions" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese New Religions">Japanese New Religions</a> are common in Brazil and Peru. <a href="/wiki/Korean_Confucianism" title="Korean Confucianism">Korean Confucianism</a> is especially found in Brazil while Chinese Buddhism and Chinese Confucianism have spread throughout the continent.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kardecism" class="mw-redirect" title="Kardecism">Kardecist Spiritism</a> can be found in several countries.
</p><p><b>Part of Religions in South America (2013):<sup id="cite_ref-latbar_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latbar-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></b>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_demographics">Ethnic demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ethnic demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_South_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic groups in South America">Ethnic groups in South America</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palenqueras_al_natural.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Palenqueras_al_natural.jpg/170px-Palenqueras_al_natural.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Palenqueras_al_natural.jpg/255px-Palenqueras_al_natural.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Palenqueras_al_natural.jpg/340px-Palenqueras_al_natural.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1530" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palenqueras_al_natural.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Afro-Colombian" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Colombian">Afro-Colombian</a> fruit sellers in <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Colombia" title="Cartagena, Colombia">Cartagena</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Japanese_Brazilian_Miko_Curitiba_Paran%C3%A1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Japanese_Brazilian_Miko_Curitiba_Paran%C3%A1.jpg/170px-Japanese_Brazilian_Miko_Curitiba_Paran%C3%A1.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Japanese_Brazilian_Miko_Curitiba_Paran%C3%A1.jpg/255px-Japanese_Brazilian_Miko_Curitiba_Paran%C3%A1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Japanese_Brazilian_Miko_Curitiba_Paran%C3%A1.jpg/340px-Japanese_Brazilian_Miko_Curitiba_Paran%C3%A1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="615" data-file-height="761" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Japanese_Brazilian_Miko_Curitiba_Paran%C3%A1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Japanese-Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Miko" title="Miko">Miko</a> during a festival in <a href="/wiki/Curitiba" title="Curitiba">Curitiba</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Festuva.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Festuva.jpg/220px-Festuva.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Festuva.jpg/330px-Festuva.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Festuva.jpg/440px-Festuva.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="399" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Festuva.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former president of Brazil Lula and members of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Brazilian">Italian Brazilian</a> community during the Grape Festival at <a href="/wiki/Caxias_do_Sul" title="Caxias do Sul">Caxias do Sul</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Quechuawomanandchild.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Quechuawomanandchild.jpg/220px-Quechuawomanandchild.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Quechuawomanandchild.jpg/330px-Quechuawomanandchild.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Quechuawomanandchild.jpg/440px-Quechuawomanandchild.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Quechuawomanandchild.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Peruvian" class="mw-redirect" title="Peruvian">Peruvian</a> woman and her son of indigenous descent</div></div></div>
<p>Genetic admixture occurs at very high levels in South America. In Argentina, the European influence accounts for 65–79% of the genetic background, Amerindian for 17–31% and sub-Saharan African for 2–4%. In Colombia, the sub-Saharan African genetic background varied from 1% to 89%, while the European genetic background varied from 20% to 79%, depending on the region.
In Peru, European ancestries ranged from 1% to 31%, while the African contribution was only 1% to 3%.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The Genographic Project determined the average Peruvian from Lima had about 28% European ancestry, 68% Native American, 2% Asian ancestry and 2% sub-Saharan African.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Descendants of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_South_America" title="Indigenous peoples of South America">indigenous peoples</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Quechuas" class="mw-redirect" title="Quechuas">Quechua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aymara_people" title="Aymara people">Aymara</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/Urarina" class="mw-redirect" title="Urarina">Urarina</a><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> of Amazonia make up the majority of the population in Bolivia (56%) and, per some sources, in Peru (44%).<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> In Ecuador, Amerindians are a large minority that comprises two-fifths of the population. The native European population is also a significant element in most other former Portuguese colonies.
</p><p>People who identify as of primarily or totally <a href="/wiki/Light_skinned_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Light skinned people">European descent</a>, or identify their <a href="/wiki/Phenotype" title="Phenotype">phenotype</a> as corresponding to such group, are more of a majority in Argentina,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> and Uruguay<sup id="cite_ref-blanca_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blanca-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> and more than half of the population of <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Chile" title="Demographics of Chile">Chile</a> (64.7%)<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> and (48.4%) in Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In Venezuela, according to the national census 42% of the population is primarily native Spanish, Italian and Portuguese descendants.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> In Colombia, people who identify as European descendant are about 37%.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Society_and_Its_Environment_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Society_and_Its_Environment-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-schwartzman_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schwartzman-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In Peru, European descendants are the third group in number (15%).<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">Mestizos</a> (mixed European and Amerindian) are the largest ethnic group in Paraguay, Venezuela, Colombia<sup id="cite_ref-The_Society_and_Its_Environment_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Society_and_Its_Environment-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and Ecuador and the second group in Peru.
</p><p>South America is also home to one of the largest populations of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic groups of Africa">Africans</a>. This group is significantly present in Brazil, Colombia, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, French Guiana, Venezuela and Ecuador.
</p><p>Brazil followed by Peru have the largest <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korean</a> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">Chinese</a> communities in South America, Lima has the largest ethnic Chinese community in Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">East Indians</a> form the largest ethnic group in Guyana and Suriname.
</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_people">Indigenous people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Indigenous people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indigenous_peoples_of_South_America" title="List of Indigenous peoples of South America">List of Indigenous peoples of South America</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_South_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous peoples in South America">Indigenous peoples in South America</a></div>
<p>In many places indigenous people still practice a traditional lifestyle based on subsistence agriculture or as hunter-gatherers. There are still some <a href="/wiki/Uncontacted_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Uncontacted people">uncontacted tribes</a> residing in the Amazon Rainforest.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">

Their language is co-official in <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>. Traditional lifestyle includes llama herding.</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Populace">Populace</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Populace">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
