<p>The most populous country in South America is Brazil with 207.7 million people. The second largest country is Colombia with a population of 48,653,419. Argentina is the third most populous country with 43,847,430.
</p><p>While Brazil, Argentina, and Colombia maintain the largest populations, large city populations are not restricted to those nations. The largest cities in South America, by far, are São Paulo, Lima, and Bogotá. These cities are the only cities on the continent to exceed eight million, and three of five in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>. Next in size are Rio de Janeiro, Santiago, Caracas, Buenos Aires and Salvador.
</p><p>Five of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_the_Americas" title="List of metropolitan areas in the Americas">top ten metropolitan areas</a> are in Brazil. These metropolitan areas all have a population of above 4 million and include the <a href="/wiki/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Greater São Paulo">São Paulo metropolitan area</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Greater Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro metropolitan area</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greater_Belo_Horizonte" title="Greater Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte metropolitan area</a>. Whilst the majority of the largest metropolitan areas are within Brazil, Argentina is host to the second largest metropolitan area by population in South America: the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Buenos_Aires" title="Greater Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires metropolitan region</a> is above 13 million inhabitants.
</p><p>South America has also been witness to the growth of <a href="/wiki/Megalopolis" title="Megalopolis">megapolitan areas</a>. In Brazil four megaregions exist including the <a href="/wiki/Expanded_Metropolitan_Complex_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" class="mw-redirect" title="Expanded Metropolitan Complex of São Paulo">Expanded Metropolitan Complex of São Paulo</a> with more than 32 million inhabitants. The others are the Greater Rio, Greater Belo Horizonte and <a href="/wiki/Greater_Porto_Alegre" title="Greater Porto Alegre">Greater Porto Alegre</a>. Colombia also has four megaregions which comprise 72% of its population, followed by Venezuela, Argentina and Peru which are also homes of megaregions.
</p><p>The top ten largest South American metropolitan areas by population as of 2015, based on national census numbers from each country:

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_(15414135738).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg/220px-Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg/330px-Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg/440px-Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1136" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_(15414135738).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Embraer_KC-390" title="Embraer KC-390">KC-390</a> is the largest military transport aircraft produced in South America by the Brazilian company <a href="/wiki/Embraer" title="Embraer">Embraer</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bodega_chakana_hacia_la_monta%C3%B1a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Bodega_chakana_hacia_la_monta%C3%B1a.jpg/170px-Bodega_chakana_hacia_la_monta%C3%B1a.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Bodega_chakana_hacia_la_monta%C3%B1a.jpg/255px-Bodega_chakana_hacia_la_monta%C3%B1a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Bodega_chakana_hacia_la_monta%C3%B1a.jpg/340px-Bodega_chakana_hacia_la_monta%C3%B1a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="4108" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bodega_chakana_hacia_la_monta%C3%B1a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Vineyard" title="Vineyard">Vineyard</a> in <a href="/wiki/Luj%C3%A1n_de_Cuyo" title="Luján de Cuyo">Luján de Cuyo</a>, province of <a href="/wiki/Mendoza,_Argentina" title="Mendoza, Argentina">Mendoza, Argentina</a></div></div></div>
<p>South America relies less on the export of both manufactured goods and natural resources than the world average; merchandise exports from the continent were 16% of GDP on an <a href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominal GDP">exchange rate</a> basis, compared to 25% for the world as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-wfex_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wfex-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Brazil (the seventh largest economy in the world and the largest in South America) leads <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_exports" title="List of countries by exports">in terms of merchandise exports</a> at $251 billion, followed by Venezuela at $93 billion, Chile at $86 billion, and Argentina at $84 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-wfex_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wfex-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 1930, the continent has experienced remarkable growth and diversification in most economic sectors. Most agricultural and livestock products are destined for the domestic market and local consumption. However, the export of <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agricultural products</a> is essential for the <a href="/wiki/Balance_of_trade" title="Balance of trade">balance of trade</a> in most countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Economy_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economy-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The main agrarian crops are export crops, such as <a href="/wiki/Soy" class="mw-redirect" title="Soy">soy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>. The production of staple foods such as vegetables, corn or beans is large, but focused on domestic consumption. Livestock raising for meat exports is important in Argentina, Paraguay, Uruguay and Colombia. In tropical regions the most important crops are <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bananas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bananas">bananas</a>, mainly in Brazil, Colombia and Ecuador. Traditionally, the countries producing <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a> for export are Peru, Guyana and Suriname, and in Brazil, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a> is also used to make <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">ethanol</a>. On the coast of Peru, northeast and south of Brazil, <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> is grown. Fifty percent of the South American surface is covered by forests, but timber industries are small and directed to domestic markets. In recent years, however, transnational companies have been settling in the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon forest">Amazon</a> to exploit noble timber destined for export. The Pacific coastal waters of South America are the most important for commercial fishing. The anchovy catch reaches thousands of tons, and tuna is also abundant (Peru is a major exporter). The capture of <a href="/wiki/Crustaceans" class="mw-redirect" title="Crustaceans">crustaceans</a> is remarkable, particularly in northeastern Brazil and Chile.<sup id="cite_ref-Economy_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economy-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Only Brazil and Argentina are part of the <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a> (industrial countries), while only Brazil is part of the <a href="/wiki/G8%2B5" title="G8+5">G8+5</a> (the most powerful and influential nations in the world). In the tourism sector, a series of negotiations began in 2005 to promote tourism and increase air connections within the region. <a href="/wiki/Punta_del_Este" title="Punta del Este">Punta del Este</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florian%C3%B3polis" title="Florianópolis">Florianópolis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mar_del_Plata" title="Mar del Plata">Mar del Plata</a> are among the most important resorts in South America.<sup id="cite_ref-Economy_80-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economy-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The most industrialized countries in South America are Brazil, Argentina, Chile, Colombia, Venezuela and Uruguay respectively. These countries alone account for more than 75 percent of the region's economy and add up to a GDP of more than US$3.0 trillion. Industries in South America began to take on the economies of the region from the 1930s when the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> in the United States and other countries of the world boosted industrial production in the continent. From that period the region left the agricultural side behind and began to achieve high rates of economic growth that remained until the early 1990s when they slowed due to political instabilities, economic crises and neoliberal policies.<sup id="cite_ref-Economy_80-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economy-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the end of the economic crisis in Brazil and Argentina that occurred in the period from 1998 to 2002, which has led to <a href="/wiki/Economic_recession" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic recession">economic recession</a>, rising unemployment and falling population income, the industrial and service sectors have been recovering rapidly. Chile, Argentina and Brazil have recovered fastest, growing at an average of 5% per year. All of South America after this period has been recovering and showing good signs of economic stability, with controlled <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a> and exchange rates, continuous growth, a decrease in <a href="/wiki/Social_inequality" title="Social inequality">social inequality</a> and unemployment–factors that favor industry.<sup id="cite_ref-Economy_80-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economy-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The main industries are: electronics, textiles, food, automotive, metallurgy, aviation, naval, clothing, beverage, steel, tobacco, timber, chemical, among others. Exports reach almost US$400 billion annually, with Brazil accounting for half of this.<sup id="cite_ref-Economy_80-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economy-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">economic gap</a> between the rich and poor in most South American nations is larger than on most other continents. The richest 10% receive over 40% of the nation's income in Bolivia, Brazil, Chile, Colombia, and Paraguay,<sup id="cite_ref-share_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-share-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> while the poorest 20% receive 4% or less in Bolivia, Brazil, and Colombia.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> This wide gap can be seen in many large South American cities where makeshift shacks and slums lie in the vicinity of skyscrapers and upper-class luxury apartments; nearly one in nine South Americans live on less than $2 per day (on a <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> basis).<sup id="cite_ref-wb2_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb2-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">Tourism</a> has increasingly become a significant source of income for many South American countries.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Historical relics, architectural and natural wonders, a diverse range of foods and culture, vibrant and colorful cities, and stunning landscapes attract millions of tourists every year to South America. Some of the most visited places in the region are <a href="/wiki/Iguazu_Falls" title="Iguazu Falls">Iguazu Falls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Recife" title="Recife">Recife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olinda" title="Olinda">Olinda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machu_Picchu" title="Machu Picchu">Machu Picchu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bariloche" title="Bariloche">Bariloche</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Lu%C3%ADs,_Maranh%C3%A3o" title="São Luís, Maranhão">São Luís</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salvador,_Bahia" title="Salvador, Bahia">Salvador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fortaleza" title="Fortaleza">Fortaleza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macei%C3%B3" title="Maceió">Maceió</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florian%C3%B3polis" title="Florianópolis">Florianópolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Ignacio_Min%C3%AD" title="San Ignacio Miní">San Ignacio Miní</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isla_Margarita" class="mw-redirect" title="Isla Margarita">Isla Margarita</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natal,_Rio_Grande_do_Norte" title="Natal, Rio Grande do Norte">Natal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lima" title="Lima">Lima</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angel_Falls" title="Angel Falls">Angel Falls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nazca_Lines" title="Nazca Lines">Nazca Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuzco" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuzco">Cuzco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Titicaca" title="Lake Titicaca">Lake Titicaca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salar_de_Uyuni" title="Salar de Uyuni">Salar de Uyuni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jesuit_Missions_of_Chiquitos" title="Jesuit Missions of Chiquitos">Jesuit Missions of Chiquitos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Roques_archipelago" title="Los Roques archipelago">Los Roques archipelago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gran_Sabana" title="Gran Sabana">Gran Sabana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">Patagonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tayrona_National_Natural_Park" title="Tayrona National Natural Park">Tayrona National Natural Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Marta,_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Marta, Colombia">Santa Marta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogotá">Bogotá</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cali" title="Cali">Cali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medell%C3%ADn" title="Medellín">Medellín</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Colombia" title="Cartagena, Colombia">Cartagena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perito_Moreno_Glacier" title="Perito Moreno Glacier">Perito Moreno Glacier</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">Galápagos Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In 2016 Brazil hosted the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Summer Olympics</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1008px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:67_-_Carthag%C3%A8ne_-_D%C3%A9cembre_2008.jpg" class="image" title="Panorama of Cartagena (2008), one of the main tourist destinations of Colombia."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/67_-_Carthag%C3%A8ne_-_D%C3%A9cembre_2008.jpg/1000px-67_-_Carthag%C3%A8ne_-_D%C3%A9cembre_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="1000" height="191" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/67_-_Carthag%C3%A8ne_-_D%C3%A9cembre_2008.jpg/1500px-67_-_Carthag%C3%A8ne_-_D%C3%A9cembre_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/67_-_Carthag%C3%A8ne_-_D%C3%A9cembre_2008.jpg/2000px-67_-_Carthag%C3%A8ne_-_D%C3%A9cembre_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="19695" data-file-height="3758" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:67_-_Carthag%C3%A8ne_-_D%C3%A9cembre_2008.jpg" title="File:67 - Carthagène - Décembre 2008.jpg"> </a></div>Panorama of <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Colombia" title="Cartagena, Colombia">Cartagena</a> (2008), one of the main tourist destinations of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>.</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:492px;max-width:492px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:89px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:2016_fachada_columnas_Teatro_Sol%C3%ADs_de_Montevideo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/2016_fachada_columnas_Teatro_Sol%C3%ADs_de_Montevideo.jpg/150px-2016_fachada_columnas_Teatro_Sol%C3%ADs_de_Montevideo.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="113" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/2016_fachada_columnas_Teatro_Sol%C3%ADs_de_Montevideo.jpg/225px-2016_fachada_columnas_Teatro_Sol%C3%ADs_de_Montevideo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/2016_fachada_columnas_Teatro_Sol%C3%ADs_de_Montevideo.jpg/300px-2016_fachada_columnas_Teatro_Sol%C3%ADs_de_Montevideo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3888" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Teatro Solis, Uruguay.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:89px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:0200_years_Biblioteca_Nacional_in_Rio_de_Janeiro_city.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/0200_years_Biblioteca_Nacional_in_Rio_de_Janeiro_city.jpg/150px-0200_years_Biblioteca_Nacional_in_Rio_de_Janeiro_city.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="99" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/0200_years_Biblioteca_Nacional_in_Rio_de_Janeiro_city.jpg/225px-0200_years_Biblioteca_Nacional_in_Rio_de_Janeiro_city.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/0200_years_Biblioteca_Nacional_in_Rio_de_Janeiro_city.jpg/300px-0200_years_Biblioteca_Nacional_in_Rio_de_Janeiro_city.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2362" data-file-height="1559" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Biblioteca_Nacional_do_Rio_de_Janeiro" class="mw-redirect" title="Biblioteca Nacional do Rio de Janeiro">National Library</a>, Brazil.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:89px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:P1060656a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/P1060656a.jpg/180px-P1060656a.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="101" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/P1060656a.jpg/270px-P1060656a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/P1060656a.jpg/360px-P1060656a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2124" data-file-height="1195" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Arya_Dewaker" title="Arya Dewaker">Arya Dewaker</a> Hindu temple, <a href="/wiki/Paramaribo" title="Paramaribo">Paramaribo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>.</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>South Americans are culturally influenced by their indigenous peoples, the historic connection with the Iberian Peninsula and Africa, and waves of immigrants from around the globe.
</p><p>
South American nations have a rich variety of <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin American music">music</a>. Some of the most famous genres include <a href="/wiki/Vallenato" title="Vallenato">vallenato</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cumbia" title="Cumbia">cumbia</a> from Colombia, <a href="/wiki/Pasillo" title="Pasillo">pasillo</a> from Colombia and Ecuador, <a href="/wiki/Samba" title="Samba">samba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bossa_nova" title="Bossa nova">bossa nova</a> and <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BAsica_sertaneja" title="Música sertaneja">música sertaneja</a> from Brazil, and <a href="/wiki/Tango_music" title="Tango music">tango</a> from Argentina and Uruguay. Also well known is the non-commercial folk genre <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Canci%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Nueva Canción">Nueva Canción</a> movement which was founded in Argentina and Chile and quickly spread to the rest of the Latin America. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"/></p><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:144px;max-width:144px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:185px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Tango-Show-Buenos-Aires-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tango-Show-Buenos-Aires-01.jpg/142px-Tango-Show-Buenos-Aires-01.jpg" decoding="async" width="142" height="189" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tango-Show-Buenos-Aires-01.jpg/213px-Tango-Show-Buenos-Aires-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tango-Show-Buenos-Aires-01.jpg/284px-Tango-Show-Buenos-Aires-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3072" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Tango" title="Tango">Tango</a> show in <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, typical Argentine dance.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:144px;max-width:144px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:185px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Carmen_Miranda_1941.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Carmen_Miranda_1941.JPG/142px-Carmen_Miranda_1941.JPG" decoding="async" width="142" height="185" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Carmen_Miranda_1941.JPG/213px-Carmen_Miranda_1941.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Carmen_Miranda_1941.JPG/284px-Carmen_Miranda_1941.JPG 2x" data-file-width="957" data-file-height="1245" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Carmen_Miranda" title="Carmen Miranda">Carmen Miranda</a>, Portuguese Brazilian singer helped popularize <a href="/wiki/Samba" title="Samba">samba</a> internationally.</div></div></div></div></div><p> People on the Peruvian coast created the fine <a href="/wiki/Guitar" title="Guitar">guitar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cajon" class="mw-redirect" title="Cajon">cajon</a> duos or trios in the most <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizo</a> (mixed) of South American rhythms such as the Marinera (from Lima), the <a href="/wiki/Tondero" title="Tondero">Tondero</a> (from Piura), the 19th century popular Creole Valse or Peruvian Valse, the soulful Arequipan Yaravi, and the early 20th century Paraguayan <a href="/wiki/Guarania_(music)" title="Guarania (music)">Guarania</a>. In the late 20th century, <a href="/wiki/Rock_en_Espa%C3%B1ol" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock en Español">Spanish rock</a> emerged by young hipsters influenced by British pop and American rock. <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Brazil" title="Music of Brazil">Brazil</a> has a Portuguese-language pop rock industry as well a great variety of other music genres.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish American literature">literature</a> of South America has attracted considerable critical and popular acclaim, especially with the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Boom" title="Latin American Boom">Latin American Boom</a> of the 1960s and 1970s, and the rise of authors such as <a href="/wiki/Mario_Vargas_Llosa" title="Mario Vargas Llosa">Mario Vargas Llosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Garc%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1rquez" title="Gabriel García Márquez">Gabriel García Márquez</a> in novels and <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Luis_Borges" title="Jorge Luis Borges">Jorge Luis Borges</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Neruda" title="Pablo Neruda">Pablo Neruda</a> in other genres. The Brazilians <a href="/wiki/Machado_de_Assis" title="Machado de Assis">Machado de Assis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Guimar%C3%A3es_Rosa" title="João Guimarães Rosa">João Guimarães Rosa</a> are widely regarded as the greatest Brazilian writers.
</p><p>Because of South America's broad ethnic mix, <a href="/wiki/South_American_cuisine" title="South American cuisine">South American cuisine</a> has African, South American Indian, South Asian, East Asian, and European influences. <a href="/wiki/Bahia" title="Bahia">Bahia</a>, Brazil, is especially well known for its West African–influenced cuisine. Argentines, Chileans, Uruguayans, Brazilians, Bolivians, and Venezuelans regularly consume wine. People in Argentina, Paraguay, Uruguay, southern Chile, Bolivia and Brazil drink <a href="/wiki/Mate_(beverage)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mate (beverage)">mate</a>, an herb which is brewed. The Paraguayan version, <a href="/wiki/Terere" class="mw-redirect" title="Terere">terere</a>, differs from other forms of mate in that it is served cold. <a href="/wiki/Pisco" title="Pisco">Pisco</a> is a liquor distilled from grapes in Peru and Chile. Peruvian cuisine mixes elements from Chinese, Japanese, Spanish, Italian, African, Arab, Andean, and Amazonic food.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plastic_arts">Plastic arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Plastic arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fernando_Botero,_Bird_(1990),_Singapore_-_20040616.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Fernando_Botero%2C_Bird_%281990%29%2C_Singapore_-_20040616.jpg/220px-Fernando_Botero%2C_Bird_%281990%29%2C_Singapore_-_20040616.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Fernando_Botero%2C_Bird_%281990%29%2C_Singapore_-_20040616.jpg/330px-Fernando_Botero%2C_Bird_%281990%29%2C_Singapore_-_20040616.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Fernando_Botero%2C_Bird_%281990%29%2C_Singapore_-_20040616.jpg/440px-Fernando_Botero%2C_Bird_%281990%29%2C_Singapore_-_20040616.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fernando_Botero,_Bird_(1990),_Singapore_-_20040616.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Bird</i> (Singapore), sculpture of <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Botero" title="Fernando Botero">Fernando Botero</a></div></div></div>
<p>The artist <a href="/wiki/Oswaldo_Guayasam%C3%ADn" title="Oswaldo Guayasamín">Oswaldo Guayasamín</a> (1919–1999) from <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, represented with his painting style the feeling of the peoples of Latin America<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> highlighting social injustices in various parts of the world. The Colombian <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Botero" title="Fernando Botero">Fernando Botero</a> (1932) is one of the greatest exponents of painting and sculpture that continues still active and has been able to develop a recognizable style of his own.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> For his part, the Venezuelan <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Cruz-Diez" title="Carlos Cruz-Diez">Carlos Cruz-Diez</a> has contributed significantly to contemporary art,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> with the presence of works around the world.
</p><p>Currently several emerging South American artists are recognized by international art critics: <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Lora" title="Guillermo Lora">Guillermo Lorca</a>&#160;– Chilean painter,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Teddy_Cobe%C3%B1a" title="Teddy Cobeña">Teddy Cobeña</a>&#160;– Ecuadorian sculptor and recipient of international sculpture award in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> and Argentine artist <a href="/wiki/Adri%C3%A1n_Villar_Rojas" title="Adrián Villar Rojas">Adrián Villar Rojas</a><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>&#160;– winner of the Zurich Museum Art Award among many others.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_South_America" title="Sport in South America">Sport in South America</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerea2_maracana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Aerea2_maracana.jpg/220px-Aerea2_maracana.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Aerea2_maracana.jpg/330px-Aerea2_maracana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Aerea2_maracana.jpg/440px-Aerea2_maracana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerea2_maracana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Maracan%C3%A3_Stadium" title="Maracanã Stadium">Maracanã Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, Brazil</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadion_Rio_de_Janeiro_Finale_WM_2014_(22117945206).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Stadion_Rio_de_Janeiro_Finale_WM_2014_%2822117945206%29.jpg/220px-Stadion_Rio_de_Janeiro_Finale_WM_2014_%2822117945206%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="98" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Stadion_Rio_de_Janeiro_Finale_WM_2014_%2822117945206%29.jpg/330px-Stadion_Rio_de_Janeiro_Finale_WM_2014_%2822117945206%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Stadion_Rio_de_Janeiro_Finale_WM_2014_%2822117945206%29.jpg/440px-Stadion_Rio_de_Janeiro_Finale_WM_2014_%2822117945206%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5485" data-file-height="2436" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadion_Rio_de_Janeiro_Finale_WM_2014_(22117945206).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Panorama of the interior of the Maracanã stadium during the closing ceremony of the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a></div></div></div>
<p>A wide range of sports are played in the continent of South America, with <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> being the most popular overall, while <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> is the most popular in Venezuela.
</p><p>Other sports include <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polo" title="Polo">polo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motorsports" class="mw-redirect" title="Motorsports">motorsports</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby</a> (mostly in Argentina and Uruguay), <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">handball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>.
</p><p>South America hosted its first <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, Brazil in 2016 and will host the <a href="/wiki/Youth_Olympic_Games" title="Youth Olympic Games">Youth Olympic Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, Argentina in 2018.
</p><p>South America shares with Europe supremacy over the sport of football as all winners in <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> history and all winning teams in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a> have come from these two continents. Brazil holds the record at the FIFA World Cup with five titles in total. Argentina and Uruguay have two titles each. So far four South American nations have hosted the tournament including the first edition in Uruguay (1930). The other three were Brazil (1950, 2014), Chile (1962), and Argentina (1978).
</p><p>South America is home to the longest running international football tournament; the <a href="/wiki/Copa_Am%C3%A9rica" title="Copa América">Copa América</a>, which has been regularly contested since 1916. Uruguay won the Copa América a record 15 times, surpassing hosts Argentina in 2011 to reach 15 titles (they were previously equal at 14 titles each during the 2011 Copa América).
</p><p>Also, in South America, a multi-sport event, the <a href="/wiki/South_American_Games" title="South American Games">South American Games</a>, are held every four years. The first edition was held in <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a> in 1978 and the most recent took place in <a href="/wiki/Santiago" title="Santiago">Santiago</a> in 2014.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/South_American_Cricket_Championship" title="South American Cricket Championship">South American Cricket Championship</a> is an international <a href="/wiki/Limited-overs_cricket" class="mw-redirect" title="Limited-overs cricket">limited-overs cricket</a> tournament played since 1995 featuring national teams from <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_South_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports in South America">South America</a> and certain other invited sides including teams from North America, currently played annually but until 2013 was usually played every two seasons.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Molino_de_viento_(moderno)_2014-09-21_(3).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Molino_de_viento_%28moderno%29_2014-09-21_%283%29.jpg/150px-Molino_de_viento_%28moderno%29_2014-09-21_%283%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Molino_de_viento_%28moderno%29_2014-09-21_%283%29.jpg/225px-Molino_de_viento_%28moderno%29_2014-09-21_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Molino_de_viento_%28moderno%29_2014-09-21_%283%29.jpg/300px-Molino_de_viento_%28moderno%29_2014-09-21_%283%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Molino_de_viento_(moderno)_2014-09-21_(3).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jepírachi wind farm in the <a href="/wiki/Guajira_Peninsula" title="Guajira Peninsula">Guajira Peninsula</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Due to the diversity of <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">topography</a> and pluviometric precipitation conditions, the region's water resources vary enormously in different areas. In the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a>, navigation possibilities are limited, except for the Magdalena River, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Titicaca" title="Lake Titicaca">Lake Titicaca</a> and the lakes of the southern regions of Chile and Argentina. Irrigation is an important factor for agriculture from northwestern Peru to Patagonia. Less than 10% of the known electrical potential of the Andes had been used until the mid-1960s.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Highlands" title="Brazilian Highlands">Brazilian Highlands</a> has a much higher <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroelectric">hydroelectric</a> potential than the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andean region</a> and its possibilities of exploitation are greater due to the existence of several large rivers with high margins and the occurrence of great differences forming huge cataracts, such as those of Paulo Afonso, Iguaçu and others. The <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon River</a> system has about 13,000&#160;km of waterways, but its possibilities for hydroelectric use are still unknown.
</p><p>Most of the continent's energy is generated through <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric_power_plants" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroelectric power plants">hydroelectric power plants</a>, but there is also an important share of <a href="/wiki/Thermoelectric" class="mw-redirect" title="Thermoelectric">thermoelectric</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wind_energy" class="mw-redirect" title="Wind energy">wind energy</a>. Brazil and Argentina are the only South American countries that generate <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a>, each with two <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_plants" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear power plants">nuclear power plants</a>. In 1991 these countries signed a peaceful nuclear cooperation agreement.
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1508px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Itaipu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Vue_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale.jpg" class="image" title="Panoramic view of the Itaipu Dam, the largest of the world in energy production."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Itaipu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Vue_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale.jpg/1500px-Itaipu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Vue_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale.jpg" decoding="async" width="1500" height="180" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Itaipu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Vue_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale.jpg/2250px-Itaipu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Vue_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Itaipu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Vue_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale.jpg/3000px-Itaipu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Vue_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10630" data-file-height="1275" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Itaipu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Vue_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale.jpg" title="File:Itaipu Décembre 2007 - Vue Générale.jpg"> </a></div>Panoramic view of the <a href="/wiki/Itaipu_Dam" title="Itaipu Dam">Itaipu Dam</a>, the largest of the world in energy production.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Avenida_General_Paz_entre_Cabildo_y_Panamericana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Avenida_General_Paz_entre_Cabildo_y_Panamericana.jpg/220px-Avenida_General_Paz_entre_Cabildo_y_Panamericana.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Avenida_General_Paz_entre_Cabildo_y_Panamericana.jpg/330px-Avenida_General_Paz_entre_Cabildo_y_Panamericana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Avenida_General_Paz_entre_Cabildo_y_Panamericana.jpg/440px-Avenida_General_Paz_entre_Cabildo_y_Panamericana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="642" data-file-height="647" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Avenida_General_Paz_entre_Cabildo_y_Panamericana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stretch of the <a href="/wiki/Pan-American_Highway" title="Pan-American Highway">Pan-American Highway</a> in Argentina</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Puerto-del-callao.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Puerto-del-callao.jpg/220px-Puerto-del-callao.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Puerto-del-callao.jpg/330px-Puerto-del-callao.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Puerto-del-callao.jpg/440px-Puerto-del-callao.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4345" data-file-height="2897" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Puerto-del-callao.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Port of Callao in Peru</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:L%C3%ADnea_Roja_de_Mi_Telef%C3%A9rico_en_La_Paz,_Bolivia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/L%C3%ADnea_Roja_de_Mi_Telef%C3%A9rico_en_La_Paz%2C_Bolivia.jpg/220px-L%C3%ADnea_Roja_de_Mi_Telef%C3%A9rico_en_La_Paz%2C_Bolivia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/L%C3%ADnea_Roja_de_Mi_Telef%C3%A9rico_en_La_Paz%2C_Bolivia.jpg/330px-L%C3%ADnea_Roja_de_Mi_Telef%C3%A9rico_en_La_Paz%2C_Bolivia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/L%C3%ADnea_Roja_de_Mi_Telef%C3%A9rico_en_La_Paz%2C_Bolivia.jpg/440px-L%C3%ADnea_Roja_de_Mi_Telef%C3%A9rico_en_La_Paz%2C_Bolivia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:L%C3%ADnea_Roja_de_Mi_Telef%C3%A9rico_en_La_Paz,_Bolivia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The La Paz cable car system in Bolivia is home to both the longest and highest urban cable car network in the world.</div></div></div>
<p>South American transportation systems are still deficient, with low kilometric densities. The region has about 1,700,000&#160;km of <a href="/wiki/Highways" class="mw-redirect" title="Highways">highways</a> and 100,000&#160;km of <a href="/wiki/Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Railways">railways</a>, which are concentrated in the coastal strip, and the interior is still devoid of communication.
</p><p>Only two railroads are continental: the Transandina, which connects <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, in Argentina to <a href="/wiki/Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Valparaíso">Valparaíso</a>, in Chile, and the Brazil–Bolivia Railroad, which makes it the connection between the port of <a href="/wiki/Santos,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Santos, São Paulo">Santos</a> in Brazil and the city of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_la_Sierra" title="Santa Cruz de la Sierra">Santa Cruz de la Sierra</a>, in Bolivia. In addition, there is the <a href="/wiki/Pan-American_Highway" title="Pan-American Highway">Pan-American Highway</a>, which crosses the Andean countries from north to south, although some stretches are unfinished.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Two areas of greater density occur in the railway sector: the platinum network, which develops around the <a href="/wiki/Platine_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Platine region">Platine region</a>, largely belonging to Argentina, with more than 45,000&#160;km in length; And the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeast Brazil">Southeast Brazil</a> network, which mainly serves the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">state of São Paulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro_(state)" title="Rio de Janeiro (state)">state of Rio de Janeiro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a>. Brazil and Argentina also stand out in the road sector. In addition to the modern roads that extend through northern Argentina and south-east and south of Brazil, a vast road complex aims to link <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a>, the federal capital, to the South, Southeast, Northeast and Northern regions of Brazil.
</p><p>The Port of Callao is the main port of Peru.
South America has one of the largest bays of navigable inland waterways in the world, represented mainly by the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_basin" title="Amazon basin">Amazon basin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Platine_basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Platine basin">Platine basin</a>, the São Francisco and the Orinoco basins, Brazil having about 54,000&#160;km navigable, while Argentina has 6,500&#160;km and Venezuela, 1,200&#160;km.
</p><p>The two main merchant fleets also belong to Brazil and Argentina. The following are those of Chile, Venezuela, Peru and Colombia. The largest ports in commercial movement are those of <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santos,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Santos, São Paulo">Santos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%ADa_Blanca" title="Bahía Blanca">Bahía Blanca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rosario,_Santa_Fe" title="Rosario, Santa Fe">Rosario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Valparaíso">Valparaíso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Recife" title="Recife">Recife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salvador,_Bahia" title="Salvador, Bahia">Salvador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montevideo" title="Montevideo">Montevideo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paranagu%C3%A1" title="Paranaguá">Paranaguá</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">Rio Grande</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fortaleza" title="Fortaleza">Fortaleza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bel%C3%A9m" title="Belém">Belém</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maracaibo" title="Maracaibo">Maracaibo</a>.
</p><p>In South America, <a href="/wiki/Commercial_aviation" title="Commercial aviation">commercial aviation</a> has a magnificent expansion field, which has one of the largest traffic density lines in the world, Rio de Janeiro–São Paulo, and large airports, such as <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo%E2%80%93Congonhas_Airport" title="São Paulo–Congonhas Airport">Congonhas</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo%E2%80%93Guarulhos_International_Airport" title="São Paulo–Guarulhos International Airport">São Paulo–Guarulhos International</a> and <a href="/wiki/Viracopos_International_Airport" title="Viracopos International Airport">Viracopos</a> (São Paulo), <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro%E2%80%93Gale%C3%A3o_International_Airport" title="Rio de Janeiro–Galeão International Airport">Rio de Janeiro International</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santos_Dumont_Airport" title="Santos Dumont Airport">Santos Dumont</a> (Rio de Janeiro), <a href="/wiki/El_Dorado_International_Airport" title="El Dorado International Airport">El Dorado</a> (Bogotá), <a href="/wiki/Ministro_Pistarini_International_Airport" title="Ministro Pistarini International Airport">Ezeiza</a> (Buenos Aires), <a href="/wiki/Tancredo_Neves_International_Airport" title="Tancredo Neves International Airport">Tancredo Neves International Airport</a> (Belo Horizonte), <a href="/wiki/Afonso_Pena_International_Airport" title="Afonso Pena International Airport">Curitiba International Airport</a> (Curitiba), Brasilia, Caracas, Montevideo, Lima,  Recife, Salvador, Salgado Filho International Airport (Porto Alegre), Fortaleza, Manaus and Belém.
</p><p>The main public transport in major cities is the bus. Many cities also have a diverse system of metro and subway trains, the first of which was the Buenos Aires <a href="/wiki/Subte" class="mw-redirect" title="Subte">subte</a>, opened 1913.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>  The <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Metro" title="Santiago Metro">Santiago subway</a><sup id="cite_ref-Home_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Home-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> is the largest network in South America, with 103&#160;km, while the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro" title="São Paulo Metro">São Paulo subway</a> is the largest in transportation, with more than 4.6 million passengers per day<sup id="cite_ref-2014ridership_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014ridership-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> and was voted the best in the Americas. In <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> was installed the first railroad of the continent, in 1854. Today the city has a vast and diversified system of metropolitan trains, integrated with buses and subway. Recently it was also inaugurated in the city a Light Rail System called <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro_Light_Rail" title="Rio de Janeiro Light Rail">VLT</a>, a small electrical trams at low speed, while <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a> inaugurated its <a href="/wiki/Line_15_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro)" title="Line 15 (São Paulo Metro)">monorail</a>, the first of South America.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In Brazil, an express bus system called Bus Rapid Transit (BRT), which operates in several cities, has also been developed.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes_and_references">Notes and references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Notes and references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Content_notes">Content notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Content notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span id="cnote_Continent_model"><b><a href="#ref_Continent_model">^</a></b></span>&#160;<b>Continent model:</b>&#160;In some parts of the world South America is viewed as a subcontinent of the Americas<sup id="cite_ref-Brasil_Emb-Mercosul_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brasil_Emb-Mercosul-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> (a single continent in these areas), for example Latin America, Latin Europe, and Iran. In most of the countries with English as an official language, however, it is considered a continent;
see <a href="/wiki/Americas_(terminology)" title="Americas (terminology)">Americas (terminology)</a>.<br />
</p>
